[944] and every time I turn around there's more of them pressing into the same space, packed tight, squeezing in, wriggling, more of them each time, more and more and more and more and more..."
==============
[945] I knelt down,
grabbed his shoulders and shook him, then did it again, hard. His head flopped back and he grabbed my wrist, a faint annoyance reaching his face. I was glad to see anything there at all.
==============
[946] I let him focus on me before saying, "There's no shadows."

He stared at me.
==============
[947] I shook my head, more sure of it now. "It's not ghosts, or a thing out there, stalking us. It _is_ us. We're what's wrong here. We're the ones who don't belong." I swallowed, bile still souring the back of my throat. "We're slipping.
==============
[948] Losing our grip on... something. This whole world, maybe. Or it's losing its grip on us."

I had his full attention now.
==============
[949] "And I don't know what happens when we let go, or it does," I finished. "But I don't think it's good."
==============
[950] He stared at me, hopeless. "There's no way back."
==============
[951] "There is. There has to be." I took a breath. "We just have to find it."
==============
[952] Chapter 7

We turned the wall of his bedroom into a map, taping up big sheets of artist's paper, shoving piles of books and unwashed dishes and dirty socks and two scuffed snowboards out of the way to make room.
==============
[953] He transferred our notebook sketches to the wall and we tried to fill in the rest from memory.
==============
[954] It was imperfect, because stairs down there ran up and down and the wall was flat, and also because the hallways twisted at weird angles and we didn't have surveying equipment to sort them out. But it was a start.
==============
[955] It was also painfully incomplete. There were dozens of doors we'd never tried, branches and halls we'd only glanced into.
==============
[956] Almost everything we had seen was from that single hall off the big room, the one we'd tried on a whim our first time down. Other than peering around the first couple corners, we hadn't explored the other four halls at all.
==============
[957] Niko swept a hand across all the empty space. "We're fucked."
==============
[958] "Look," I countered, "we know the other versions of us found a key, somewhere. And we also know the two sides are staying almost exactly in sync. Close enough to spill coffee the same way."
==============
[959] "Not close enough to leave each others' fucking sticky notes alone."
==============
[960] "Still," I pressed on, "that means the keys can't have been too well-hidden. We could have almost found one, walked right past it. Maybe the only difference was a momentary decision about which door to go through, what wall to glance at."
==============
[961] "Doesn't matter." He stirred his coffee, morose, and sat it down to cool on his dresser, next to a half-empty older mug growing a skim of mold. "The keys are useless now, anyway."
==============
[962] "If there's one set of keys, there might be more. Other keys, other doors. And besides, we have no idea what else might be down there. We need to keep looking."
==============
[963] He ran a hand through his hair, a familiar gesture, but he looked changed. His eyes were getting sunken, from lack of sleep or some more worrisome deficiency. His face, so often laughing, hadn't smiled in days.
==============
[964] "Synchronicity," he said. "That's the problem."

"How do you mean?"
==============
[965] "I think we're getting out of sync with them. Day by day, decision by decision, we're losing our lockstep. And the farther out of sync we drift, the harder it gets to go back."

"Speculation."
==============
[966] "And the deeper," he pressed on, "the deeper we'll have to go to find another way through."
==============
[967] "Bullshit." But I didn't have energy to argue with him. Clearly we couldn't solve anything from up here. We needed to go back down. We had to fill in the blank spaces on that map.
==============
[968] Our first expedition departed the next morning. We had backpacks, trail mix and energy bars, lots of flashlights and batteries, twine, spray paint, a compass, graph paper, whistles, and rope.
==============
[969] Despite everything, I think the prep got us fired up a bit. If answers were down there, we'd find them. We skipped class and I called in sick to work, and we both agreed if necessary we'd do the same tomorrow, and the next day.
==============
[970] Finding a way back was top priority.
==============
[971] "They're not _our_ grades anyway," Niko said with a smirk. I sensed a slippery slope here vis-à-vis morality and nihilism, but I wasn't in the mood to debate philosophy with him. I wanted to move. To delve. Find some answers.
==============
[972] We chose one of the unexplored halls off the big room, and decided to explore as much of it as we could, until we'd mapped it all or got too tired to keep going. We picked the one at the far end of the room, opposite the stairs back up.
==============
[973] Right away we found something different.
==============
[974] The first few twists and turns were like the rest of the top level: carpet, wall sconces, scuffed doors.
==============
[975] But after a short and confusing snarl of hallways and tiny rooms, the floorplan opened up into an area with brighter lights in the sconces, and longer, straighter hallways.

Except some of them went straight down.
==============
[976] We stood at the lip of one of these pits and stared over the edge. It was like someone had taken a regular hallway and stood it on end.
==============
[977] The brown carpet went right over the lip and continued straight down, passing sideways doors, sideways wall sconces.
==============
[978] Maybe seventy or eighty feet down, it hit a carpeted bottom and leveled out again, branching in opposite horizontal directions.
==============
[979] The pit filled the exact center of a junction; we could step around the corners into hallways leading off in the three other directions from the one we'd arrived. It was a five-way intersection, all at right-angles.
==============
[980] A couple dozen paces down one of those halls was another pit.

"What is this," Niko sighed, "challenge mode?"
==============
[981] When you think of treacherous terrain a basement hallway isn't the first thing that comes to mind, but clutching the corner and peering vertiginously down, the pit looked as unscalable as the Matterhorn.
==============
[982] There was nothing to get a grip on, except the doorways every twenty feet or so. Clearly we couldn't get down without climbing gear, nor come back up without it either.

If you fell... if you got stuck down there...
==============
[983] We stepped carefully around the pit and kept exploring on the same level. But the pits were everywhere. Each horizontal hall would dead end sooner or later, and the side rooms were all small and empty.
==============
[984] Some of them had hallway pits, too, leading down from their exact center. After an hour we'd mapped out everything we could get to without a climbing harness.
==============
[985] Other than going back to the big room, there was no way forward except fourteen pits, each at least fifty feet deep.
==============
[986] "Difficult could be good." He perked up. "This is the first thing we've had to work for. Maybe means there's something interesting down there."
==============
[987] "Or maybe one of the other hallways leads to a room filled floor to ceiling with keys. No point guessing."
==============
[988] We went back to explore one of the other halls---we didn't have much choice---and found something different there, too. About half the doors led not to rooms, but to crawlways.
==============
[989] They were those half-sized doors you find sometimes that open onto water heaters or the electric meter in your house.
==============
[990] Flush with the floor and about three-and-a-half feet tall, they opened onto similarly miniaturized corridors, snaking off in two directions for a dozen feet with T-junctions at each end.
==============
[991] Niko leaned casually against the door and poked his head inside with a suave expression. "Hey," he said to the crawlway, "How _you_ doin'?"

We figured out pretty quick it was a maze.
==============
[992] You could stoop-walk, but crawling on all fours was a lot more comfortable. (For me, at least. Niko kept bumping his head and swearing.) The tiny hallways branched and split constantly, keeping to neat ninety-degree angles.
==============
[993] Those ever-present wall sconces remained brightly lit, but the crawlway never went the same direction for long. Doors were scarce, and they all led back to normal-sized halls.
==============
[994] Once we realized how easy it would be to get lost, we retraced our steps and sat panting by the entrance.
==============
[995] "Promising," Niko said. "They're making us work for it."
==============
[996] "There's no 'they,'" I said automatically, mostly because I didn't want to think about it. "And it's the same problem again. We can't risk getting lost down here."
==============
[997] "But this is easier, man. We don't need specialized equipment. Just some way to leave a path. Hansel and Gretel, like you said."
==============
[998] Or maybe Ariadne. I had a ball of twine in my pack, so we settled for a simple solution: tying one end to my ankle, and the other around the half-door's knob.
==============
[999] After some deliberation, we decided to keep our packs on, despite the awkwardness of crawling the tunnels with them. Having girded ourselves with stuff, we felt naked without it now.
==============
[1000] We set off to map. It wasn't long before we found another, even tinier door.
==============
[1001] This one was no more than eighteen inches high. Peering inside it, we saw an even smaller crawlway, with even smaller doors running up and down its length.

"That's some Alice in Wonderland shit right there," Niko muttered.
==============
[1002] We could maybe have squeezed into the next level of smaller crawlways without our packs, but there didn't seem to be much point. Maybe the crawlways could get fractally smaller, but we couldn't.
==============
[1003] We decided to stick to the first tier of crawlways and map out their extent.

What happened next caught us completely unprepared.
==============
[1004] We'd started crawling in a promising direction. I'd begun to feel almost cheerful: we were solving the mystery, peeling back this place's secrets. Surely it was just a matter of time before we found a way back home.
==============
[1005] Something _yanked_ my ankle from behind.
==============
[1006] I gasped and twisted around. The twine tied to my ankle was taut, and pulling me with terrible force, starting to drag me back the crawlway. I cried out, digging my fingers into the carpet.
==============
[1007] The twine scraping against the edge of the junction behind us sounded coarse and ugly, like a rusty knife dragged over the hairy skin of a coconut.
==============
[1008] "What the fuck, _help me!_" I shouted. The loop around my ankle was viciously tight, cutting off circulation. My fingers scrabbled for purchase but the carpet wasn't shaggy enough to grip.
==============
[1009] Niko scrambled back towards me, shrugging out of his pack and grabbing my arm. But as he pulled me back the twine dug into my ankle like a vise, like the pressure would saw the line straight through my foot. It _hurt_.
==============
[1010] I couldn't understand why it hadn't snapped. "Cut it, fucking cut it!" I gasped.
==============
[1011] He cursed and let me go, whipping back around to zipper open his pack, letting the line start to drag me away. The sound of the twine scraping the corner seemed way too loud, like someone was holding a mike against it.
==============
[1012] I reached up to grab a wall sconce and the cheap thing twisted off in my hand, sparking as the bulb went out. I held onto it stupidly as the line around my ankle dragged us both away, reeling out drywall-dusted power cable from the wall.
==============
[1013] I panicked. My mind flashed through visions of monsters waiting just around the corner, reeling me in. A horned demon. Some evil-eyed little girl from a shitty horror movie.
==============
[1014] And then the history lady flashed into my head, inside-out and distorted past the breaking point, eyes white and wide;
==============
[1015] and I jabbed my fingers into the grooves in the fake wooden wall paneling and started babbling

 SURELY NO HOPE LEFT

mind slipping towards the only place it might be safe

 How a child wishes
 To live down there!
==============
[1016] and Niko cut the twine.
==============
[1017] I missed the lead-up in my nightmare, but he'd dug through his pack for the Swiss army knife, lost at the bottom with the camping gear, then struggled to squeeze ahead of me without kicking me in the face.
==============
[1018] He told me later he'd barely touched the blade to the twine when the taut line snapped, whipping around the corner in a fraction of a second.
==============
[1019] He had to spend a minute calming me down. My mind had skidded toward some rarely glimpsed drop-off, pulled edgeward by a dark and primal gravity, and it took time to climb handhold by handhold back up to the light.
==============
[1020] What brought me back, prosaically enough, was the growing unpleasant tingling in my foot. Pins and needles: painful, but familiar.
==============
[1021] The knot on the twine had slipped down and pulled a tight loop around my leg just above the ankle, digging half an inch into my jeans. Niko helped me cut it off and I sat rubbing my foot for a long time, calming down, waiting.

Listening.
==============
[1022] After maybe fifteen minutes we started back, Niko up front with the knife. I was equally terrified bringing up the rear, though, constantly looking over my shoulder, miserable and afraid.
==============
[1023] The fact that the lighting was so bright and consistent, so cheery, only tinged my fear a more metallic shade.
==============
[1024] Around the corner we found the cut end of the twine, slack and unmoving. We followed it all the way back to where we'd come in.
==============
[1025] It was no longer tied to the doorknob, like we'd left it. The twine lay coiled up in a neat loop. Right outside the threshold.
==============
[1026] Chapter 8

"So this is huge," Niko was saying. We were in the funny-shaped room behind the closet with the never-to-be-completed board game, dust gathering on unresolved plans for world domination.
==============
[1027] We'd moved all our expedition gear in here; we didn't want to explain things to anyone else, and the rest of the housemates had forgotten this room even existed.
==============
[1028] I rubbed the ugly bruise ringing my ankle, sitting on the grimy hardwood floor with my pant leg rolled up.
==============
[1029] "Oh yeah?" I winced, prodding a tender spot.
==============
[1030] "It's the first concrete sign there's something down there. Not glints of light. Not sounds. Something physical."

"Yeah, reassuring."
==============
[1031] He conceded the point, slumping down next to me. "But why now? What brought this on? Is the maze forbidden? Did we violate some kind of policy?"

"Marking our way."
==============
[1032] "What?"
==============
[1033] I sniffled. "It's the first time we've tried to leave a permanent trail, something unambiguously marking the way back. Maybe whatever it is... ugh." It still felt awful to verbalize it, give it that kind of legitimacy.
==============
[1034] "Maybe it didn't like that."
==============
[1035] "Or maybe whatever's down there doesn't want us exploring the crawlways. Because they lead to something. Something big."
==============
[1036] I punched the wall, suddenly angry. "Who knows? None of it makes any sense anyway."
==============
[1037] "That'll go on our tombstones. A week from now, when we're dead of fucking dimension poisoning."
==============
[1038] "Well hey, dude, it's either that or lung cancer thirty years from now." I mimed taking a drag off a smoke. "At least dimension poisoning's probably quicker."
==============
[1039] He laughed despite himself, and I chalked up a mental win. Cheering him up, making him smile, was so ingrained in me I barely noticed I was doing it any more. Maybe that day, I shouldn't have been.
==============
[1040] It wasn't exactly a situation to be cheerful about.
==============
[1041] _Do I do it because I really want him to be happy? Or is it that I can't stand it when he's sad?_

"I'm not going down there again," he said with grim finality.
==============
[1042] Neither of us said anything for a long minute.
==============
[1043] "Okay fine, I am. You're right. You win. We find a way back. Somehow."

"There's monsters up here, too," I said softly.
==============
[1044] He sniffed. "Or maybe we're the monsters, man. Crawled out from underneath the bed."
==============
[1045] * * *

We decided to explore the vertical shafts, instead of going back into the crawlways. We didn't know whether what had happened was a message or a provocation. I thought the bruises on my ankle were message enough: Keep Out.
==============
[1046] Niko argued that was exactly why we should ignore it. Wherever they don't want you to go is probably the most interesting place to be. On the other hand, maybe the message had been like fences around Chernobyl.
==============
[1047] Maybe what was farther in was worse.
==============
[1048] So we settled on the shafts, which were unusual and promising terrain without even mild signs of demonic infestation. One of Niko's ex-hobbies was rock climbing, but he'd stopped after the accident jacked up his wrists.
==============
[1049] Bits of gear still lingered around his overstuffed bedroom, though, so we'd assembled some rope, harnesses, carabiners, and a couple of grappling hooks from the sporting goods store.
==============
[1050] The box called them "Grip Monkeys," which seemed incongruously cheerful.
==============
[1051] We picked the first pit, since they all seemed about the same, and set about securing the grapples in a doorjamb in a way that would hold our weight. We'd each go down on our own rope, one at a time and using the second as backup.
==============
[1052] We also had extra Grip Monkeys in our pack, in case something happened to these.
==============
[1053] Along with the usual gear, we also brought down a camcorder. We were too broke to afford the newer all-digital cameras, so we borrowed one that shot on Hi-8 tape.
==============
[1054] This was before the whole found footage craze, so we didn't think to take the camera down the pit with us and record weepy confessionals into it: we were going to leave it down the hall from the shaft,
==============
[1055] trained on the pit and our ropes and the Grip Monkeys, hopefully capturing anything that tried to mess with us.
==============
[1056] When we were ready, and since we didn't have a tripod, I left the camera on the floor a dozen paces back, pointed at the pit, and hit record. We shouldered our packs and Niko tied on to the rope.
==============
[1057] Moving carefully, he stepped over the lip, and started to rappel down the carpeted "floor" of the shaft. I watched his grapple nervously, but it held his weight, tines set deep into the solid wood of the door frame.
==============
[1058] The bottom of the shaft seemed a mile down with Niko dangling above it, but probably only dropped about seventy feet. He moved fast and soon was stepping onto the once-again-horizontal carpet at the bottom.
==============
[1059] He shined his light back up at me and gave the all-clear.
==============
[1060] I followed him down, trying to think only in particulars about what was happening and not the terrifying big picture. I focused on old climbing lessons, what my hands were doing. One thing at a time. Presently I'd made it down too.
==============
[1061] The hall at the bottom of the pit stretched off to either side, like we were at the junction of an upside-down T. Detaching from our dangling ropes, we picked a direction and began to explore.

Things got weird down there.
==============
[1062] The hallways continued on as they had above, and there were more pits. But these didn't go straight down. Not quite. They descended at angles ranging from severe to subtle, never quite true to vertical. Some were almost ramps.
==============
[1063] Others changed their angle or gradually twisted as they dropped. And while the pit we'd rappelled down was lit, none of these were. They each plunged down into darkness.
==============
[1064] And there were more of them. A lot more. Hundreds. Most opened from the middle of a hallway, filling its width: easy to jump across, but wearing a pack you felt clumsy, were acutely aware you were one stumble away from a very bad time.
==============
[1065] We decided to avoid any unnecessary leaps, but the pits were so thick they hedged us in, pushed us inexorably towards an unknown destination.
==============
[1066] If we tried to veer too far off course, they'd get denser, and we'd have to backtrack or turn aside, angling back to our former heading. And the longer we followed it, the more the hallway angles edged off true.
==============
[1067] It was subtle at first. But the horizontal hallways were getting less and less level. We'd stumble on a floor that canted slightly left, or tilted half a degree up or down.
==============
[1068] The walls, too, were growing angled, some leaning outward a degree or two instead of staying neatly parallel, or bent a little bit inward at mismatched angles. It made us feel drunk.
==============
[1069] You've seen so many well-constructed hallways in your life, your brain doesn't know how to process ones that don't behave.

We kept going.
==============
[1070] The halls branched and spread out endlessly. We gave up trying to map, other than our route back. We passed through regions of dark and regions of light. The decor rarely varied from its ubiquitous blandness.
==============
[1071] Sometimes little things were wrong. A door, off its hinges, lying neat and flat in the center of the hall. A light fixture sticking out of the carpet. Crown molding running in a line a foot above the carpet.
==============
[1072] We searched around these anomalies, but never found anything useful.
==============
[1073] Some of the rooms got larger, too big for rooms in a house. More like a school gymnasium. Still the same carpet, though. And it felt like we were seeing more of the anomalies, the farther in and deeper down we got.
==============
[1074] Doors or sections of hallway paved in bathroom tile; weird cube-shaped extrusions or cavities in the edges of rooms. It was like the deeper we went, the more flexible the rules became---of architecture, of stability, of god knows what else.
==============
[1075] We were getting tired. Just before turning back, though, we found one last curious room. We could hear it before we opened the door.
==============
[1076] The room was the size of a squash court, though not quite as tall, the whole thing covered in green bathroom tile, even the inside of the door we came through. A sink rose serenely from its center.
==============
[1077] Scalding water blasted from the faucet, releasing clouds of billowing steam and filling the air with a moist, sticky warmth.
==============
[1078] The sink was full, water spilling over its sides and flowing down the porcelain like some artsy fountain, then streaming away across the tile, presumably according to some imperceptible tilt in the floor.
==============
[1079] It vanished down an open hallway, carpeted once again, slanting down at a steep angle from a corner of the room.
==============
[1080] We walked over to the hallway to peer down. It was closer to vertical than horizontal, dropping at a vicious angle.
==============
[1081] Where the hot stream hit the tilted carpet it became black with mold, and the walls and ceiling of the tunnel were stained with rust and moss. Like water had been coursing through it for a long, long time.
==============
[1082] From the slanting darkness rose a hot smell of rot.

"This feels different," Niko said.
==============
[1083] We walked back to the sink and tried to turn off the faucet, but the hot and cold knobs spun loose. The scalding water rushed full force out of the tap, churning noisily in the basin.
==============
[1084] "We're going to have a hell of a water bill," I joked, but then remembered something. The newspaper article from the history lady, about the boys lost in the cave whose entrance had once been on the site of our house.
==============
[1085] The spring that bubbled up from beneath it. The spring that had been bricked up.

Looking-Glass Cave.
==============
[1086] I felt as if something was on the verge of snapping into place, making sense. But I couldn't quite see it.
==============
[1087] We can see our coloured faces
 Floating on the shaken pool

I got down on hands and knees to stare into the running water, not sure what I expected to see. But there was nothing.
==============
[1088] The billowing steam and rippling of the water meant I couldn't even see my own reflection.

I got to my feet, feeling deflated.
==============
[1089] Niko was beaming his flashlight down the tunnel, chasing the descending path of the stream. "This would be rough going. Steep and slick. We'd need better climbing gear. And I can't see how far down it goes."
==============
[1090] I took a deep breath. "It feels like that's the way, though. Doesn't it?"
==============
[1091] He ran a hand through steam-wilted hair, eyes still pulled down the shaft. "Jesus, I hope not."
==============
[1092] * * *

I couldn't stop thinking about the wet tunnel as we retracted our steps. Images of it flashed through my mind. The thought of what might be past the reach of our flashlight beams, what was down there, was maddening.
==============
[1093] I was planning how soon we could come back down, what we'd have to bring with us. What it would take to keep pushing deeper.
==============
[1094] We passed through the last few hallways to the base of shaft we'd come down. On the carpet directly underneath were our ropes, coiled up neat, Grip Monkeys still tied to the end.
==============
[1095] "God damn it," Niko said with feeling, craning his head to glare accusingly at the shaft and fling curses up its length. We couldn't see anything unusual up there, not from down here.

Our way back up had been cut off.
==============
[1096] We had extra grapples in our packs, but the originals didn't seem damaged: just detached. The shaft was too narrow to throw one all the way back up without hitting a wall, so we settled for hooking a doorway, halfway up.
==============
[1097] Our position now was much more precarious. We couldn't tell if the grapple was set properly: we just had to trust it. Niko volunteered to go first. From the ground below, I watched him climb, anxious.
==============
[1098] And for some reason, that was the moment I finally accepted that I was still in love with him. I'd tried so hard to convince myself I wasn't, that I'd moved on, wrung him out of my heart, that all we had was an especially deep friendship.
==============
[1099] But watching him dangle from that rope, knowing he could fall at any second, I couldn't pretend any more. I'd never stopped loving him. I didn't know how. Maybe I never would.
==============
[1100] And that was also the moment the grappling hook ripped through the molding of the wooden doorframe far above, and Niko fell.
==============
[1101] Chapter 9

Time seemed to snap and twist back on itself in opposing directions, both too fast and too slow.
==============
[1102] Terror struck me like lightning, searing me with unbearable matching thoughts: _he's going to die_ and _there's nothing I can do to help him_.
==============
[1103] Then he grabbed the edge of the next doorframe down and his body slammed against the horizontal door beneath. I watched the bottoms of his sneakers as they kicked and flailed at the smooth beige wall, scrabbling for purchase.
==============
[1104] He was still too far up. _Too far._ If he fell...
==============
[1105] "Are you okay?" I shouted up at him, or something equally useless. My lungs were clenched so tight that for a minute I couldn't breathe back in.
==============
[1106] He'd managed to press the toes of his sneakers up against the wall, but there was nothing to stand on. His position was desperate, hands gripping the inch of molding like claws. I could see muscles trembling even from here.
==============
[1107] He clung to the wall quivering like a caught-out insect, paralyzed with indecision.
==============
[1108] "You're okay." I tried to keep my voice light, in control, willing confidence into it and up to him. My mind thrummed as it raced to find him a way out.
==============
[1109] He was still clipped on to the climbing rope but the grapple now swayed useless beneath him.
==============
[1110] The hallway pit ran featureless above and below the doorframe he clung to: there was nothing else to get a grip on, not for a dozen feet in either direction.
==============
[1111] "The door." I projected calm authority. "You need to get the door open. If there's a room inside, it'll only be a little drop. Niko. Are you listening to me?"
==============
[1112] He shook his head, as if snapping out of shock, found the doorknob beneath him and focused on it. It was on the bottom side of the door from our perspective, at waist-height for Niko, but too far off to the side to easily reach.
==============
[1113] He lifted an ineffectual foot to try kicking at it, but it was too high. I watched his fingers slip towards the edge of the molding.
==============
[1114] "Nice idea." I tried to keep my voice steady. "Just try again, okay? I'm right here. If you fall, I've got you." But did I, really? My arms were stretched out stupidly, but if he fell into them from that height it would break us both.
==============
[1115] He kicked again, more desperate this time, foot still far from the knob. His shoe scudded across the smooth paint of the door. His fingers gripped the molding so tight they'd gone white. He couldn't hold a grip like that much longer.
==============
[1116] "You almost had it," I lied. "Come on, buddy, you got this."
==============
[1117] "Just shut up for a second," he shouted, flashing a glare down at me. "Stop fucking telling me what you think I want to hear and shut up."
==============
[1118] I fell silent, face flushed, paralyzed. Singed.

He stared at the knob, and the silence sharpened until I couldn't help but break it, to say out lout what I knew he was thinking.
==============
[1119] "You'll have to let go with one hand." I said it as even as I could. "Just for a second. To turn the knob." I breathed. "There's no other way."
==============
[1120] He nodded. I stood helpless below him, arms still stretched up, aching.

Then he did it.
==============
[1121] In one quick move he pressed his body in toward the door, letting his toes take as much weight as they could, let go of the frame with his left hand and thrust it out hard toward the knob.
==============
[1122] He brushed it and for a horrible moment it looked like he wouldn't be able to grip it and turn it, the angle all wrong, and so was his balance, now; but then his fingers wrapped around the knob, his wrist twisted and it turned.
==============
[1123] The door clunked and swung inwards from the bottom as his weight pushed against it, and he half-collapsed, half-scrambled through as his balance was lost, fingers slipping off the frame.
==============
[1124] He tumbled inside, banging knees and shins, and fell through, the door swinging shut behind him like a cat flap, muffled thumps and curses making their way through the walls.
==============
[1125] But before I could even breathe out, a shock of awful, sawtoothed sound smacked into me from above, and I was so startled I bit my tongue.
==============
[1126] It was utterly alien, a juddering metallic _twang_ that lingered in the air, throbbing, jittery, reluctant to die away.

And then I realized what it was.
==============
[1127] The sound turned in an instant from monstrous to mundane. Niko must have thwacked it as he tumbled past, flailing: one of those springy metal doorstoppers, no doubt surprised to meet a falling body instead of a hastily opened door.
==============
[1128] * * *

We made it to the top, in the end.
==============
[1129] It took a series of shorter climbs to each sideways room, treating them like miniature base camps, places to rest before flinging the grapple up another dozen feet to the next door, the next cube of safety;
==============
[1130] testing each set of the grapple more thoroughly, belaying each other as best we could in the patently unsafe circumstances.
==============
[1131] But at length, we'd made it back out.
==============
[1132] "Sorry about earlier. What I said." I'd just grabbed his hand pulling me up the last few feet, and now we were sprawled on the carpet, mercifully horizontal again, like two mountaineers on the world's blandest summit.
==============
[1133] "Don't worry about it. You just... do that sometimes, and it bugs me." _Tell him what I think he wants to hear._ I shut my eyes. "I wish you'd..." He lifted a hand, gestured vaguely in the air, dropped it in defeat. "Whatever, forget it.
==============
[1134] There's a million more important things to worry about."

The camcorder was where we'd left it, sitting on the carpet pointed at the pit.
==============
[1135] The door frame where our original grapples had been attached wasn't damaged. We'd seated them pretty firmly, so this suggested that rather than being yanked free from below, someone had carefully unhooked them from up here.
==============
[1136] Of course, the ropes had also been neatly coiled at the bottom. Someone had to have done that from down there.
==============
[1137] Niko didn't want to watch the tape, not while we were still Downstairs. But I couldn't stand not knowing. So he huddled miserably beside me while we watched the footage on the tiny flip-out screen.
==============
[1138] The tape had run to the end, so we backed it up a bit and hit play. To our dismay, the ropes were going over the edge right to the end; whatever happened, it had been after the tape ran out.
==============
[1139] Niko held down the rewind button and we settled in for a long haul: but after only a few seconds we saw ourselves spring back up from the pit in fast motion, first me and then him;
==============
[1140] dicker with the grapples and rope for a few minutes; then zip over to the camera to turn it on.
==============
[1141] "I swear the tape was at the beginning," Niko said. "There should have been two hours of space. This is like five minutes at most. What the hell?"
==============
[1142] He let go of the rewind button and let the tape play.
==============
[1143] We watched in numb frustration as everything we'd done earlier played back: the same discussions about rope and seating the grapples, the same lame jokes failing to ease tension. There wasn't much point to watching it all unfold again.
==============
[1144] We just didn't know what else to do.
==============
[1145] On the tiny screen, I was standing a pace or two back, wondering aloud how much stuff we should take down with us. I hated how my voice sounded on tape, how my face looked. I always had. Even on the tiny screen I could see red blotches.
==============
[1146] On the screen a miniature Niko sat on the edge of the pit, adjusting his ropes.

Distorted by the shitty camcorder speaker, he said, "How far down do you think this goes?"
==============
[1147] My image shrugged, said "We could possibly go much deeper."
==============
[1148] My skin crawled. "Oh my god."
==============
[1149] Niko glanced at me. "What?"
==============
[1150] "That's not what I said." My head was spinning. What _had_ I said? Something like _It can't possibly go much deeper_, maybe. Not that.
==============
[1151] Screen-Niko said "You're right. Actually, we shouldn't you and I come back this route at all. We should go deeper and we should let's stay down, down and deep." His voice sounded strained, but he pulled his rope tight smartly.
==============
[1152] "Don't come back up until we find it, Ry. What it is we need to find."
==============
[1153] Where it gripped the camcorder, Niko's hand was pale. "I didn't say that either," he breathed. "I mean I said something about that long, some of those words and phrases maybe.
==============
[1154] But they're _different they're fucking different---_"

I shushed him, because the voices on the tape were speaking again. But now the words were familiar, mundane.
==============
[1155] We both watched the screen, afraid to blink, but nothing else seemed changed. Everything played out as we remembered. Except now every word and gesture caused a spike of uncertainty. _Had_ I said that, exactly that?
==============
[1156] Had I moved my arm that way, stood in precisely that spot?
==============
[1157] Screen-Niko started to rappel. The camera focused on my legs as I stood up top, watching him descend. On the screen I waited, then clipped onto the rope once he'd made it to the bottom.
==============
[1158] Screen-Ryan checked his harness, took a deep breath, and started down.
==============
[1159] He paused before his head dropped out of frame to call down to Niko: "Coming down." I remembered saying that.

Then he turned and looked straight at the camera.
==============
[1160] Straight into the lens.

He held the gaze for a long moment.
==============
[1161] Then he glanced, deliberate, down the shaft. Then back to the camera.

Wide-eyed.
==============
[1162] His head dropped out of sight.

We sat frozen, watching the video of the empty hall for another thirty seconds, until the tape reached its end and clunked to a stop.
==============
[1163] Niko breathed out. "Jesus." He closed the screen and sat the camera down, backing away from it like it was a bomb. "Jesus fucking Christ."
==============
[1164] I kept staring at it. CAVE SEARCH CALLED OFF floated through my head, the headline from the old newspaper article. SURELY NO HOPE LEFT FOR YOUNG SPELUNKERS.

Pools as clear as air.
==============
[1165] "Jesus," he kept muttering. "Jesus."
==============
[1166] * * *

We slept in the big room that night because we always had low-level headaches now when we went upstairs. (Also, because I thought I heard someone up there, rummaging in the kitchen. The housemates were all supposed to be at a party.
==============
[1167] "Hello?" I'd called, but no one answered. The noises stopped, though.) We were becoming trolls, hiding from sounds, afraid to go out under the sky, only venturing from our cave to get more supplies, stock up for further ventures down.
==============
[1168] I slept under the foosball table, gathering dust. No one but us had been down here for weeks.

It won't surprise you to hear I had nightmares.
==============
[1169] I replayed the tape in my dreams, over and over. Each time I rewound all the way to the start, intent to watch it through, make sure there wasn't some clue I'd missed. And each time the tape was different.
==============
[1170] It was always Niko and the pit and I, but never the same. And whenever something changed, fresh dread flooded through me.
==============
[1171] Sometimes the changes were slight, barely there, and I struggled to catch the altered words, the different glances.
==============
[1172] Sometimes our words were rearranged, as if to make cryptic cyphers, buried meanings on the verge of making sense but never quite resolving.
==============
[1173] In some of these variations, Niko and I were boyfriends. A couple. I could tell from the words we used, the way we looked at each other. Nothing that would have been obvious to anyone but me.
==============
[1174] I replayed these scenes over and over, rewinding to catch the little glances, secret smiles.

There were other, worse versions.
==============
[1175] There were dream-tapes where a gaunt Ryan and Niko fought each other for control of the camera, staring manic into the lens with frantic mouths full of rotting teeth,
==============
[1176] skin flaking beneath torn and faded rags sticky with dried blood, like they'd been trapped down there for months.
==============
[1177] They clawed at the lens, as if trying to climb into it. As if it somehow were a way back out.
==============
[1178] There were tapes where we cursed out our watcher-selves, told them to go away, to never come back again, that what was down there would destroy us.
==============
[1179] There were others, far worse, where we laughed like sharks, invited ourselves to come down there, and stay.
==============
[1180] There were versions where the grapple failed and Niko or I fell, the sound of a sickening crunch reverberating up the shaft. There were versions where we looked right into the lens and stepped willingly off the edge.
==============
[1181] There were versions where the carpet turned soft and we sunk into it like quicksand, Niko screaming while I smiled until fibers closed over my head. There were versions where hurricane winds sucked us screaming into the pit.
==============
[1182] And on one tape---and I rewound and re-watched this over and over, in the dream---water from all the hallways poured into the pit, a four-sided waterfall.
==============
[1183] The carpets were black and sticky with moss trailing down into the vertical shaft, the walls not smooth and white but rocky like cave tunnels, the air thick with steam.
==============
[1184] Something jostled the camera and it surged forward with the tide, water sloshing against the lens, until the scalding stream carried it over the edge and it fell,
==============
[1185] straight down into that boiling pit, surrounded by water on every side, gathering speed, falling into wet and steaming dark, faster and faster and faster...
==============
[1186] I would jerk awake at this point, coated in sweat, and try not to fall back asleep. But when I did I'd find myself rewinding the tape yet again and pressing play, hoping this time the footage would return to normal.
==============
[1187] It was always changed, and I'd have to watch it all over from the beginning, hoping this time I'd catch something useful, a hint, a clue, an answer.
==============
[1188] * * *

I woke to the smell of stale nicotine. Niko leaned against the stairs back up to my room, staring into the dark, a lit cigarette between his fingers.

"Our lease says no smoking in here," I grunted, still shaking off nightmares.
==============
[1189] He took another drag. "Blow me."
==============
[1190] I laughed and he flashed me a wicked grin. It felt good to laugh. Even if it was a little bit forced, to make sure he knew that I knew he was kidding.
==============
[1191] Rubbing my eyes, I sat up in my sleeping bag. After a moment I scrunched over beside him, back against the stairs.

We steeped in smoke and silence for a long minute.
==============
[1192] "Did I ever tell you," he finally said, "about that time I went camping by myself, up in Brushwillow?" I shook my head. "Used to do that a lot, after the, uh. Accident."
==============
[1193] I took that in. He hadn't brought it up in a long time. Neither had I.
==============
[1194] "I went by myself, cause I didn't want a lot of people around just then, and it's easier than twisting people's arms to get them to come with you. Planning around schedules, all that bullshit." He shifted into citation voice.
==============
[1195] "'If a man goes alone, he might leave today; but if he travels with friends, he must wait till each one is ready.'"

"Yeah, Thoreau. You quote that one a lot."
==============
[1196] He shrugged. "I like it up there. Anyway."

I waited, staring into the whorled beige universe of the carpet.
==============
[1197] "So this one night I'm up there, alone. I'm in my tent, and it's dark. Cloudy, no moon. I'm sleeping fine, on my back, you know, head up against the edge of the tent. And then I wake up, cause I hear something, just outside."
==============
[1198] He sucked on the cigarette. "Something breathing. Low, hissing, gurgling breathing. Sounded huge, like a bear or something, a big-ass wolf. And it was right on the other side of the tent flap. Inches from my face.
==============
[1199] Like something had pressed its muzzle against the nylon, that thin nothing sheet of ultralight fabric, and was waiting. It could smell my breath, maybe. Waiting for me to move. And as soon as I did, it would get me.
==============
[1200] "I still remember what that felt like. Fucking terrifying.
==============
[1201] "I was too scared to move, so I lay there a long time, hoping it would go away. But it didn't. The thing stayed where it was. Kept making those horrible breathing sounds. Inhale. Exhale. Raspy, choking."
==============
[1202] He dropped the cigarette into an empty soup can we'd brought down as an ashtray.
==============
[1203] "And then I realized where the sound was coming from. The breathing was coming from me. I was sleeping on a root or something, my head had gotten into some funny angle. I was snoring, basically, and woke myself up.
==============
[1204] But I didn't realize what woke me was a sound I was making myself."
==============
[1205] I was too tired to process this. "Cool story."

"Do you get what I mean, though?"
==============
[1206] I rubbed a hand over my face, tried to think.
==============
[1207] "You're saying maybe there's not... a _thing_ down there. That somehow, all of it is us."
==============
[1208] "Echoes," he said. "Reflections. The rooms are reflections of our shitty old house, and the things we're seeing, experiencing down there, maybe they're not alive. We're causing them, somehow.
==============
[1209] And now we're ascribing intentionality to side effects. Jumping at our own shadows." He lay back down on his sleeping bag, staring up at the ceiling.
==============
[1210] I remembered something from a neurobiology class. "Did you know there are more neurons going from your brain to your eyes than in the other direction?"

"So?"
==============
[1211] "From your brain to your eyes," I repeated, "not the other way around."
==============
[1212] He blinked. "That doesn't make sense."
==============
[1213] "It does if you realize that vision is mostly the brain telling the eyes what it expects them to see." I rubbed my face again, trying to wipe off the exhaustion. "We think we have two little cameras in our head. We don't.
==============
[1214] They're little yes-men, reassuring us nothing unexpected is happening. That's why that trick works, with the guy in the gorilla suit. You ever see that video in school?"
==============
[1215] He nodded. "You're watching a bunch of people toss a ball around, and the guy in the gorilla suit walks right through them, and it's like he's invisible. He even waves. But you don't see him the first time, because you're watching the ball.
==============
[1216] Then you watch it again looking for him and your mind's blown." He smiled faintly. "Dude in my high school science class swore the teacher changed the tape."
==============
[1217] "You don't see the gorilla because you don't expect to. There's no reason he'd be there, so your eyes don't notice him. Even though he's in plain sight. Standing right in front of you."

We were both quiet for a while.
==============
[1218] "So maybe we're somehow looking at this wrong," I finally said. "We're not seeing something. We keep saying it doesn't make any sense. Maybe we're just not seeing it the right way."
==============
[1219] "Maybe." He closed his eyes. "Or maybe there's nothing there to see."
==============
[1220] "Niko." I swallowed. "You think our doubles are the same as us? Like, exactly the same?"
==============
[1221] "Obviously not," he said, rolling over. "They found different things. Made their own fucking video."
==============
[1222] "That's what I mean." My stomach felt unsettled. I was on the verge of saying something dangerous. He felt it too. I could tell just from looking at the back of his head. "Little differences. Other versions of us. Of everything.
==============
[1223] Where there's no three dollar bill. Who knows. Maybe there's versions where both of us, where one of us..."
==============
[1224] "Go to bed, man. We need to get some fucking sleep."
==============
[1225] We both closed our eyes and tried.
==============
[1226] I could feel the camcorder dream lingering, eager to take over again. I tried to fight it off, but I was so tired.
==============
[1227] "Even if we are the wolf," Niko muttered, just as I was about to drift off, "that doesn't mean it's not trying to kill us."
==============
[1228] * * *

I tried to take a midterm and it was a disaster. I hadn't been to class in weeks, which didn't help, but everything I'd learned earlier had vanished from my brain, neurons reclaimed, I supposed, for more important things.
==============
[1229] Then I started hallucinating, questions and pencil marks multiplying and layering on themselves even when I looked up from the test,
==============
[1230] abstractions filling the darkened auditorium, and I had to flee, whispering a hurried apology to the T.A. that I was having a medical emergency.
==============
[1231] He told me to go home and take care of myself. I was halfway home before I remembered that phrase has a positive meaning, too.

I'd thought he was telling me to commit suicide.
==============
[1232] Something was in my room when I got back. I stood outside the closed door, dried blood on my face, listening. It sounded like an elephant. Heavy, clopping footfalls made the floorboards groan. Wet, agitated breathing rasped.
==============
[1233] Dust motes danced at my feet in a strange breeze, sucked under and pushed back out through the space below the closed door, rhythmic. Air moved with faint fleshy sounds, like a hundred quiet people flapping their arms, flailing.
==============
[1234] I crept away, miserable, and by the time I came back with Niko and he threw open the door in some play at courage, there was nothing there.
==============
[1235] I collapsed into his arms, sobbing, and he let me stay there for a while until I'd calmed down. I clung to him, afraid if I loosened my grip he'd disappear. Like dad, tucking me in. Gone between one blink and the next.
==============
[1236] He had a perpetual headache now. He kept describing it with the word "throbbing" and only that word, as if clinging to the sound of it.
==============
[1237] Like using a different one would acknowledge the pain too had changed, grown worse, was no longer caged by the word he'd picked to trap it. I could see how much it hurt him to think, to make words, to move around. He ground his teeth.
==============
[1238] He stood up carefully now, putting a hand against the wall each time, as if his blood was fighting his heart's attempts to lift it to his head, to keep it from being dragged back down.
==============
[1239] My headaches were getting worse, too, but it wasn't the pain that bothered me. It was the strain of always having them that wore on me. Of wondering if I'd have to deal with them for the rest of my life.
==============
[1240] * * *

We left to explore down the slippery tunnel late that night.
==============
[1241] It might have made more sense to leave after a good night's rest, but neither of us could sleep, and spending so much time down there meant night and day were becoming academic concepts anyway.
==============
[1242] Niko caffeined up (I was jittery enough already), and we loaded our packs with canned food and power bars, thick gloves, and crampons from the sporting goods store. "12 points of contact ensures solid grip on ice," the box had said.
==============
[1243] We didn't expect the manufacturer had tested them on slime-covered carpet, but it was the best we could do.
==============
[1244] In my pack was also a gun. I bought it from a place I'd driven past every day on my way to work but never gone into until that morning. The friendly clerk agreed to waive the mandatory waiting period in exchange for the last of my ATM cash.
==============
[1245] I didn't tell Niko about the gun. I thought it would make me feel safer but it just felt heavy.
==============
[1246] It had been a hot day and the old house clung to that heat through the night with grim brick desperation. Descending into chillier air was a relief. With every step down the headaches diminished, our mood improved.
==============
[1247] It was almost addictive, being down there.
==============
[1248] We retraced our route through the upper halls to the top of the shaft and reset the grapples. This time Niko hammered them into the doorjamb, face set, until he'd driven the steel spikes three inches into the wood.
==============
[1249] Even so, neither of us really expected they'd still be there when we got back.

When, or if.
==============
[1250] Getting down was a familiar exercise now, danger mitigated by procedure and repetition. We retraced our route to the tiled room with the sink.
==============
[1251] The water was still running, hot and steaming, rushing across the floor to the corner with its angled hallway lined with slimy black carpet.
==============
[1252] We shined our lights down the hot throat and the steam grabbed their brightness, bounced it back to us innocently. We couldn't see more than a few body lengths down.
==============
[1253] Niko ran a hand through his curls, deflating again in the hot moist air; scratched the hair behind his ear furiously, like a dog with an itch. "Are we sure about this? Really really?
==============
[1254] Because it sort of seems like a colossally stupid thing to do."

"You have a better idea?"
==============
[1255] He sighed, looking down the steaming shaft unhappily.

"No, I don't have a better idea," he said at last.
==============
[1256] We pulled on the crampons and the heavy gloves. Harness, rope, knots. Check. Niko pounded two new Grip Monkeys into either side of the angled tunnel entrance. We tied on. Double-check.
==============
[1257] Then, each holding our rope, kicking hard to sink the sharp toes of the crampons deep into the slimy carpet, we started down.
==============
[1258] It was slow, hot work. Once we got inside the slanted hall, the steam was oppressive, everywhere: we were instantly drenched with it, like rot-smelling sweat. Even with the crampons our feet slipped.
==============
[1259] The sludge was deep and slick, a stew of algae and mold and fungal slimes, green-black and stinking of putrefying jungle, of horrible things happening under your carpet, inside your walls. We held tight to the ropes with steam-wet gloves.
==============
[1260] The walls and floor twisted and bent as we descended, as if the constant moisture had warped them, but the downward angle stayed vicious.
==============
[1261] It was a gullet. We were letting ourselves be swallowed. No---worse. We were forcing ourselves in. Eager. Like we couldn't wait to be digested.

We were nearing the end of our sixty meter ropes when everything went to shit.
==============
[1262] All at once we were sliding. Our ropes had gone slack in our hands, no longer connected to anything. There was no time to dig in the crampons; we were already moving too fast, careening down like a grotesque slalom.
==============
[1263] Neither of us screamed, focused I guess on trying to grab hold of something, anything, but there were no doorways, no light fixtures, nothing but the thick hot slime and the scalding water.
==============
[1264] I tried to dig my feet into the oozing carpet but my loose rope had entangled me, my pack was in my way, my face was smeared with scalding gunk and I couldn't open my eyes.
==============
[1265] My hand closed on Niko's leg and I grabbed it. A moment later the floor angle shifted and he cried out, threw his body sideways, brought us both to a shuddering, squelchy stop.
==============
[1266] We were soaked through, overheating. Scalding water ran past us down the slope. I blinked my eyes open and saw he'd wedged himself into a kink in the tunnel.
==============
[1267] One of his knees was scraped open and a dull red mark on his forehead was beginning to swell. But he'd done it. He'd stopped us.
==============
[1268] Ropes slithered down the tunnel past us, followed moments later by two grapples still tied to their ends.
==============
[1269] Niko reached out to grab one with his free hand, but his weight shifted, and he had to throw the hand back against a wall to re-brace, cursing. I tried to snag them with my foot, but didn't even come close.
==============
[1270] They vanished down the tunnel, trailing rope.
==============
[1271] Niko's face was tight. He tilted his head down toward me. "This was a mistake. God, we're so fucking stupid. Ryan, man. We have to go back."
==============
[1272] "Hang on," I gasped, head filled with the roaring of the water, blinking gunk from my eyes. "Don't panic. We can do this."
==============
[1273] "Man, I'm barely holding on. I don't know how much longer I can keep from slipping. We have to try to climb back up."
==============
[1274] "Back?" I said, confused. "You want to go back?"
==============
[1275] He stared down at me. "Of course back. Are you fucking crazy? Where the fuck else?"
==============
[1276] "There's nothing good up there. Nothing right." I kicked my foot for purchase, managed to rest at least some weight on a hidden protuberance. "Besides, nothing's changed. The plan's still the same.
==============
[1277] This is the best lead for finding a way back to our side."
==============
[1278] "Are you not paying attention?" he hissed, furious. "Something is trying to kill us."
==============
[1279] "So let's find out how to stop it." I tried to keep my tone reasonable. "We're halfway down already. Climbing back up will be hard, regardless. Why not get all the way to the bottom first?"
==============
[1280] "Because we don't even know if there is a bottom." His face was blotched red with fury, with sweat, with the scorching heat of the air. "Halfway? We have no fucking idea how deep this goes. I should have said this a long time ago.
==============
[1281] You're obsessed. You get obsessed a lot, man, let it drag you down. Your stupid records." He took a deep breath. "Well now you're obsessed with this place, and it's blinding you. It's _feeding_ on you, your obsessions. Multiplying them.
==============
[1282] You can't see it, or maybe you don't want to, but I do. I'm looking right at it. Like the gorilla in the crowd."
==============
[1283] I was angry. "If I'm obsessed with anything, it's with finding a way back. We're running out of time. We either figure this out, or we're stuck here forever, in the wrong world. We need each other to get through this."
==============
[1284] I said it again, like saying it could make it true. "We need each other."
==============
[1285] "You're obsessed with me, too," he muttered. "When was the last time you hung out with someone else?"

"When was the last time you did?"
==============
[1286] He shook his head angrily, dismissing this.
==============
[1287] "Our housemates," I pushed, "when was the last time you hung out with any of them? Anyone other than me?" He stared back, seething. "Their names. I bet you can't even remember their names." I was bluffing. But could I remember them, either?
==============
[1288] Names, faces. No. There was nothing. None of those people mattered, not to me, not to us. We were the only thing that mattered. Getting back to where we'd been, what we'd had. What I'd wanted.
==============
[1289] He shook his head again, violent, like there was something inside it he wanted to dislodge. "You're living in a fantasy," he spat, "you always have been. _I can't be what you want me to be, okay?_
==============
[1290] I can't be what anyone fucking wants me to be. You all have these versions of me in your head, these ideal perfect Nikos, but they're not real. I can't live up to them." He opened his eyes, stared yearningly back up the shaft. "Help me.
==============
[1291] If you really care about me, help me back up. Don't be like everyone else. Don't just fucking _use_ me to get what you want."
==============
[1292] "Going back's not going to help. There's no answers up there." He wasn't understanding. I reached for something else. "Those headaches aren't going away. You think you can live with that pain? Forever?"
==============
[1293] "Better than being fucking dead!" He seemed to realize I wasn't changing my mind, turned away to reach for a handhold, but there was nothing there, nothing to grip, and he scrabbled pathetically at the slime.
==============
[1294] "Is it?" I shouted, angry, desperate. I had to say something, something that would make him stay, keep him here, and my mouth raced ahead of me. "You won't make it, up there, not with pain like that. We both know you won't."
==============
[1295] He tensed, glared down at me. "What the fuck is that supposed to mean?"
==============
[1296] "You know exactly what it means," I said, shaking. "Never really helped you. I've done nothing but help you. I've always been there for you. Every fucking time you fall I pick you back up. _You'd be dead if it weren't for me._"
==============
[1297] He shot me with a gaze of such cold fury I cringed. "You're fucking poison," he hissed, "you know that? A fucking snake. I wish you'd let me die that night. I wish we'd never met. _Let go of me!_"
==============
[1298] And his hand did close on something, and he pulled himself up, triumphant.
==============
[1299] His leg was slipping out of my hands, and I couldn't bear for him to crawl away from me, couldn't handle the thought of going back up to that world, to any world where everything was wrong and nothing I wanted was possible, so I pulled.
==============
[1300] I pulled, too hard, and both his hands slipped, and he crashed back into me, only I wasn't holding onto anything but him any more so both of us tumbled down,
==============
[1301] faster and faster, slipping and twisting and scraping together down the steepening blood-hot slope, down and down and down into darkness.
==============
[1302] PART TWO

MULTIPLICIOUS

From "Dark Pines Under Water," Gwendolyn MacEwen (1941-1987):

"But the dark pines of your mind dip deeper
And you are sinking, sinking, sleeper
In an elementary world;
==============
[1303] There is something down there and you want it told."
==============
[1304] Chapter 10

The first time someone kissed me it didn't really count.
==============
[1305] I'm in the closet at the back of the band room, sophomore year of high school, and this annoying girl, Krissy or Kristy or something,
==============
[1306] has followed me in to grab the music stands, and she's especially giggly and flighty and nervous for some reason,
==============
[1307] brushing up against me, and then the lights switch off and she grabs me and I realize it's a setup, she got someone to stay out there and flip the switch: and in the sudden gloom she grabs me and crushes her lips against mine.
==============
[1308] And all I can think of in this moment is Bradley, this cute sweet transfer student who a month before had found out I also liked weird old music, so he corners me after band one day to talk about it.
==============
[1309] He loves old music, strange music, making weird cross-genre mix tapes, and he plays some for me out of the half-dozen he keeps in his backpack, which is also filled with loose-leaf sheets of staff paper scribbled with notes because oh,
==============
[1310] he also composes, too, and he's impossibly cute and I'm so flustered, embarrassed, because as obvious as his interest seems now, back then it's not even possible for me to consider it.
==============
[1311] I never once think that he might be like me because I've never met anyone like me.
==============
[1312] We spend hours in the practice room and make plans to hang out again and then the next day in the hall some kid from the varsity team shoves him to the ground, hard, sends his books flying. Calls him a faggot.
==============
[1313] I'm paralyzed, half a hallway away, frozen while I watch Bradley say something from the ground, a denial, maybe, and the jock is saying something back, evidence, maybe, but I can't hear because my pulse is pounding in my ears.
==============
[1314] I'm too afraid or ashamed to go help him, to say anything at all, risk the ugly spotlight of the jock's face turning on me, too, because he's clearly making a thing of this, drawing a line. Not in our school.
==============
[1315] I imagine a chalk outline around Bradley, red graffiti. A queer died here.
==============
[1316] I can't move, not even when he finishes collecting his things, gets up, and walks away, taunts at his back, walks down the hall towards me,
==============
[1317] and now I can move but only to turn away, face flushed and heart galloping, and I can't look at him and I don't know if he sees me there as he passes by.
==============
[1318] But he isn't at school the next day and the week after I hear he's transferred somewhere else, and I never see him again.
==============
[1319] And now in the dark closet as this dumb girl's lips push against mine all I can think is that it should have been Bradley, my first kiss should have been him, and now I've fucked it up, lost it,
==============
[1320] failed him and myself and even this girl, whose eyes I can't meet either as I pull away and brush past her out of the closet and past snickering faces to the door outside, changed, maybe, or maybe not.
==============
[1321] Her hair was in the way, after all, long straight blonde strands of it tasting like strawberry conditioner, so our lips didn't really even touch, let alone tongues. Was that a kiss? Did it count? Who knows.
==============
[1322] I don't feel like it should, and anyway I don't feel any different except maybe worse, somewhere deep down, even less experienced and less ready and less sure of who I'm supposed to be. I drop out of band not long after that.
==============
[1323] I've always liked listening to music more than playing it, anyway, and I like to listen alone.
==============
[1324] * * *

I plunged into a pool of steaming hot water, instantly immersed, choking. My scrabbling hand found something slimy but solid and pushed against it. My face broke the surface and I gasped, slipping and struggling to my feet.
==============
[1325] Water came up to my waist. I wiped rank muck off my face, blinked burning eyes open, tried to catch my breath.
==============
[1326] It was utterly dark. All I could hear was splashing water.
==============
[1327] "Niko?" I shouted.

Nothing.
==============
[1328] I shrugged off my pack, zipped it open with blind, shaking fingers while struggling to keep it above the waterline, and fumbled around inside. My hand closed on a plastic tube. Glowstick. I pulled it out and snapped it, shook it, frantic.
==============
[1329] A dim blue glow began to bring the world back, a breath at a time. Churning water was everywhere, white and frothy. Steam swayed. A few steps away a sheer angled shaft climbed back up, lined in oozing black gunk and coursing fluid.
==============
[1330] The one we'd slid down, presumably. Turning all the way around, the edges of my dim circle of light suggested level hallways, flooded, leading off into darkness in three equidistant directions.

No sign of Niko.
==============
[1331] Something dark and coiling swirled in the water: my rope. I grabbed for it and reeled it in. One end was still attached to my waist. At the end of the other, my shiny grappling hook trailed tangled green streamers.
==============
[1332] I searched the frothing surface, but saw no sign of a second grapple, or a second rope.
==============
[1333] Shutting my eyes, I tried to sort through the confusion of the sliding fall. We had tumbled, together at first, my hands grabbing for his slime-drenched shirt, the sodden edges of his pack. But there was nothing to get a grip on.
==============
[1334] After those first few moments all I could feel was my own tangled rope, the pasty mulch sliding past me. I assumed I'd gotten ahead of him, or behind.
==============
[1335] But what if I hadn't? What if he'd managed to stop himself again behind me, wedged himself into another kink in the tunnel?

Or what if the tunnel had split, somewhere up there?
==============
[1336] I didn't want to think about the third possibility, but I spent a few grim minutes duck-walking through the water, old rescue swim lessons running through my head, feeling my hands through the muck beneath the churning surface.
==============
[1337] I found nothing solid. No backpack, no rope. No body.
==============
[1338] He wasn't here. I was alone.
==============
[1339] Everything in my pack was soaked. I threw out a waterlogged sandwich and watched it drift in the churning current before vanishing beneath the foam, as if someone hungry underneath had grabbed it.
==============
[1340] I'd lost a crampon in the fall and couldn't find it, so I took off the other one and maneuvered it into my pack. The blue light from the glowstick turned everything the same shades. Black and blue.
==============
[1341] I had no idea if the dripping gun would still work, and was seized by a thick fear now of firing it down here---of how far that sound would carry and what it might attract---but I slipped it into my belt anyway.
==============
[1342] It still didn't make me feel safe but I tried to pretend it did.
==============
[1343] My flashlight wouldn't turn on, even with fresh batteries. "Water resistant," according to the package, but I imagined it had been subjected to an environment outside factory test conditions.
==============
[1344] I strapped it to the top of my pack anyway, hoping it might dry out and be useful again. I had a dozen waterproof glowsticks, so I wasn't really worried about light.

Not yet, anyway.
==============
[1345] I stared up the shaft we'd tumbled down for a long time, considering. Climbing back up---without a rope, with only one crampon, without someone helping me---seemed impossible.
==============
[1346] I tried to picture Niko up there somewhere, struggling to pull himself back up, handhold by slippery handhold. If he made it to the top, he'd throw another rope down to me.

Wouldn't he?
==============
[1347] I waited a long time, as long as I could stand it. It might have only been a few hours, maybe even less. But it grew more and more maddening to simply stand there, soaked through, bathed in steam and sweat, doing nothing.
==============
[1348] Wondering if he was trying to find me. Wondering if he'd left me behind. Wondering if he was drowning or dead or lost, somewhere in this maze.
==============
[1349] At last I decided to move. If he'd made it back up, he could take care of himself. And if he was down here somewhere, maybe I could find him. Offer help, if he needed it. If he'd take it.
==============
[1350] Anyway hadn't I said it would be silly to make it all the way here and not explore?
==============
[1351] It was the deepest we'd been yet. Maybe there were answers down here. Or at least another way out.
==============
[1352] I picked a flooded hallway, took out my keys and gouged a crude arrow into the shitty paint of the wall, drywall dust spilling out. Breadcrumbs, to find my way back.
==============
[1353] Or show Niko where I'd gone, if he was lost down here too, or came looking for me.

_And if something else comes looking, you're pointing it right at you._
==============
[1354] But there was nothing to be done about that. I gave the shaft back up one last doleful look, then turned to the hallway and began to push my way forward through the hot, sluggish water.
==============
[1355] * * *

I wandered. I'm not sure for how long. The black water's surface smoothed once I moved away from the turbulence at the bottom of the shaft, swallowed up the glowstick's dim blue light.
==============
[1356] There were no longer any curious features or unusual architecture: only an irregular grid of junctions. The infrequent side rooms were always empty.
==============
[1357] Sometimes the floor or ceiling sloped up or down, not always in sync; so the water level would drift from ankle-deep to above my waist, and the ceiling from claustrophically low to beyond the reach of my light.
==============
[1358] The halls trended wider and narrower, too, in unpredictable rhythms. I worried for a while about stepping into a pit I couldn't see and dunking myself again, but there weren't any. Nor were there stairs, up or down, or even light fixtures.
==============
[1359] Only hallways, branching, recombining, endless.
==============
[1360] The air stayed steamy, and while the water cooled as I moved farther from the hot inlet stream it was still uncomfortably warm. I felt hot and clammy, thick-headed.
==============
[1361] Mist swirled in the air, sculpting the dim blue light into strange shapes and shadows.
==============
[1362] I kept gouging arrows into the wall with a key, kept moving. If I kept moving I wouldn't have to stop, wouldn't have to think.
==============
[1363] Walking takes almost no thinking at all.
==============
[1364] * * *

I came to another spot where the hallway widened, but this was different. Running along the indentation in one wall was a row of pay phones.

I slowed to a stop and stared, wondering if they were really there.
==============
[1365] They rose from knee-deep water, six of them each on its own steel pole.
==============
[1366] The ceiling had risen so high my glowstick couldn't find it, but light stabbed down from somewhere, spotlighting each phone like it stood beneath its own personal streetlight, fierce and bright after hours of flat blue glow.
==============
[1367] Water sloshed as I trudged over to the nearest phone, reluctant but intrigued. Pay phones don't normally live inside a house. Did that mean something?
==============
[1368] I touched the black plastic of the receiver. It felt grimy and cold. As if in a dream, I lifted it, held it to my ear.

Dial tone.
==============
[1369] I blinked as it droned in my ear. This didn't make sense. If there was no power this far down, surely there weren't phone lines either.
==============
[1370] Some telecom grunt hadn't run a cable all the way down here, snaking it through all these endless halls and vertical shafts, had they? Hope they billed by the hour.

The sound of the dial tone was uncomfortably familiar.
==============
[1371] Without meaning to, I reached out a finger and dialed a number from an old commercial jingle. Seven sing-song digits.

A voice told me to insert fifty cents.
==============
[1372] I almost laughed at this familiar banality. I slapped my pockets, but had no change. I hadn't expected to need any.

I put down the receiver, lifted it again and dialed zero, still not really expecting anything would happen.
==============
[1373] After a ring, a woman's voice: "Operator."
==============
[1374] My bluff had been called. I didn't know what to say. "Er... I'd, uh, like to make a collect call."
==============
[1375] "Please hang up, dial star nine seven, then the number you wish to call. Say your name at the first tone."

"Thanks," I managed.
==============
[1376] She was gone. The silence hung oppressive in her absence. I needed a voice back on that line. With a couple words she'd made the familiar loneliness unbearable.
==============
[1377] But who could I call? Water sloshed around my knees as I considered the utter inexplicability of my situation. Should I call the police, explain I was lost in my own basement, miles from the surface?
==============
[1378] Ask the fire department to send a rescue team through my bed, down the vertical hallway, and throw a rope ladder into the slimy tube in the giant bathroom?
==============
[1379] Or maybe I'd call a friend. You know, one who'd believe me, who wouldn't hang up thirty seconds into my story. In the movies, whenever someone says "You wouldn't believe me if I told you," there's always someone to say back: "Try me."
==============
[1380] This person invariably turns out to be surprisingly open-minded.
==============
[1381] I knew with grim certainty this was not going to work for me. The only friend I had like that was Niko. And he was gone.

I felt desperately alone.
==============
[1382] My fingers brushed against the dial pad, hesitating. They punched star nine seven and then kept going, tracing out a familiar pattern, a groove deep in muscle memory. My fingers knew it well.

At the first tone, I said my name.
==============
[1383] Something clicked and whirred in the receiver. A pause, and then, a ring.

Another.
==============
[1384] Another.

Someone picked up and said, "Hello?"
==============
[1385] "Mom." Relief flooded through me like adrenaline. You trust a voice like that on a primitive level, instinctual, in parts of your brain deeper than logic, than thought.
==============
[1386] She must have heard something in my tone. "Honey? What's wrong?"
==============
[1387] "What, I only call you when something's wrong?" I tried to joke, but my eyes were tearing up and my hands were trembling. I held the phone tight against my face. It smelled like old sweat and institutional cleaner.
==============
[1388] With my other hand I wiped my forehead. Swallowed. "Nothing's wrong. Just wanted to hear your voice. How are things? Tell me what you're up to." I didn't care what she said. I only wanted her to talk and keep on talking.
==============
[1389] To hear sounds from a normal world and pretend I was part of it. That I'd ever been part of it.
==============
[1390] She humored me for a minute, but I could tell she was worried. And I couldn't think of anything to say that would get me out of here.
==============
[1391] "Alright, star man," she finally said, and my brain flashed to my sixth birthday when she dressed up like an astronaut to bring in my cake. Crêpe paper planets and glow-in-the-dark comets. "Fess up. What's going on?"
==============
[1392] "I'm... I'm in trouble, mom." My voice was breaking. "Something's happened. You remember my... my friend Niko?" I rushed forward, babbling. "I've lost him, mom, I don't know where he is, where either of us are.
==============
[1393] I fucked things up and I don't know what to do. This is too big, all of this is too big, and I... I made a mistake, and..."
==============
[1394] I bit my lip so I'd stop talking, something pressing down hard on my chest, and gripped the phone like it was my last anchor to reality. Maybe it was.
==============
[1395] She took a deep breath. Let it out.
==============
[1396] "Oh, honey," she said. "Is it... is it AIDS?"
==============
[1397] Of all the things to be terrified about right then, that one was so far down the list that my brain sort of tripped over itself, downshifted straight back to first and stalled the hell out. "Oh," I said. "Uh. What? No. No, it's not AIDS.
==============
[1398] Mom. I wouldn't tell you something like that over the phone." I took a deep breath, and once again said something I probably shouldn't have. I said it with deadly seriousness. "It's HIV."

There was an awful silence.
==============
[1399] Then I started giggling. I couldn't help myself.
