==============
[1400] "That's not funny, Orion," she said, but then she was laughing too, and neither of us could stop, even when she kept trying to, kept saying "Orion" again in her serious voice which just set me off more, which set her off again too.
==============
[1401] And if I could have given anything to stretch that moment out forever, I'd have done it in a heartbeat.
==============
[1402] I wiped tears from the corners of my eyes. "I'm sorry. No, it's not that. I can't really explain it. I guess I just needed to hear your voice more than anything. I'll... figure something out."
==============
[1403] "That's my smartie." I could picture her expression when she said this; she'd said it a lot. "You're sure it's nothing I can help with?"
==============
[1404] "I'm sure." The blue monochrome of the glowstick made the pay phone into an artsy abstraction; the blackness around me sucked away all the rest of its light.
==============
[1405] "Well, you'll figure it out. You always have, even when... when there wasn't someone there to help you." She took a deep breath. That was a big thing for her to admit. "You know you can always ask for help when you need to.
==============
[1406] But you won't always need to. And that's okay."
==============
[1407] Tears were pushing out of my eyes again, damn it. I leaned against the booth, screwing them shut. "Thanks, mom," I whispered.
==============
[1408] "I love you, sweetie," she said. "Do you want to talk to your father?"
==============
[1409] And out of everything that had happened, all the unexplained and terrifying and gut-wrenching things, nothing hit me like those words did. Sometimes words hit harder than a slap. You feel them, like ten thousand volts.
==============
[1410] They sour everything that came before, ruin everything coming after. That's how those words hit me.

Because my father was dead.
==============
[1411] "No," I managed in a quiet, trembling voice.
==============
[1412] "Oh, he's right here, honey, it's no trouble. Hang on."

I stood clutching the phone, unable to move, to breathe.
==============
[1413] Faint rustling sounds came over the line.

"Well hey there, son."
==============
[1414] This is something you probably won't understand unless you've lost a parent. You have to put things away when that happens. Something is gone and parts of you went with it, in ways that aren't always obvious.
==============
[1415] You have to accept that this person is not coming back. You may not want that to be true but it is and you can't change it, and you need to believe you can't change it, which isn't quite acceptance, but still. You do it.
==============
[1416] You put the pain from those missing pieces in a box and nail it shut and you don't forget it or accept it, not exactly, but you learn to stop thinking about it. After a while it's almost like you've buried the box, or lost it. It's gone.
==============
[1417] And then you hear that voice again, and you realize nothing was ever buried or lost or even nailed shut. The box has been there all along, wide open, and everything in it still has exactly the same power to hurt you.
==============
[1418] It's just been waiting for the right moment to try.

"Hey, dad."
==============
[1419] The words came out against my will. _There's been a mistake_, I thought dreamily. He's still alive.
==============
[1420] Just a dream that a freight truck doing ninety smashed into him on a country highway with a busted stoplight, killing him instantly, taking him away from me between one blink and the next. It made sense: it had never felt real, anyway.
==============
[1421] Some strange multi-year delusion, not easy to explain but so, so easy to accept.

Or maybe in this universe it had never happened.
==============
[1422] _Maybe here, he's still alive._
==============
[1423] This had never once occurred to me since I'd passed through to this side. It was too huge a change. All the differences were so tiny, so inconsequential. Not like this.

_Or._
==============
[1424] _Maybe it's not him at all._
==============
[1425] Something inside me withdrew, to wherever small animals go in their heads while staring down looming headlights. Some residual part of me thought I ought to move, speak, react. Get out of the way. But I didn't know how.
==============
[1426] "Good to hear your voice." My dad. He sounded like he meant it. "How you holding up?"
==============
[1427] "Dad." I wasn't in control: I sounded distant to myself, like someone else was speaking. "Dad. What's going on?"
==============
[1428] He chuckled. "We were going to ask you the same question. Your mother and I were a little worried after that call the other day."
==============
[1429] I couldn't think. "Call?" I said stupidly.
==============
[1430] "From you and Niko." My father hesitated. "We couldn't figure it out, son. You want to let us in on the gag?"
==============
[1431] "Uh. Gag?"
==============
[1432] "Sure. All that business about _going deeper_."
==============
[1433] My blood was frozen and my mouth had gone dry. "What?"
==============
[1434] "You said," he explained, voice still achingly familiar, "you both said the next time you called, I was supposed to remind you that you have to go deeper." He cleared his throat. "That, um."
==============
[1435] I could hear the rustle of a paper, like he was reading off a notepad. I could see him, squinting through his glasses. "That you're not deep enough yet, and you need to keep going. Deeper and deeper. As deep as you can get."
==============
[1436] He cleared his throat. "Pretty mysterious. What's it all about?"

The ground felt like it was dropping away.
==============
[1437] "So what's the news, son?" my father said, a hint of a smile in his voice. "You in deep enough yet?"
==============
[1438] I dropped the phone. It swung on the end of its metal coil, spinning slowly. I could still hear his voice, faint and distorted---

"Ryan?"
==============
[1439] ---dad's voice, drifting faint from those tiny holes in the receiver, as I backed away, staring---

"Orion? Are you there?"
==============
[1440] ---and my shoulders hit the wall, and I couldn't back away any more but I could still hear his voice coming out of the receiver, so I pulled out my gun and shot it.
==============
[1441] Somehow I hit the dangling receiver on my first shot, and it exploded. Tiny bits of plastic shrapnel cut the air. One whizzed past my cheek and sliced it open. I didn't notice.
==============
[1442] I raised the gun to the boxy metal body of the phone and shot that, too. I shot it again and again until the gun wouldn't fire any more.
==============
[1443] My ears hurt. The reverberations were deafening, echoing endlessly.
==============
[1444] I pictured compressed sound waves expanding through miles of hallways, like a dangerous thought lighting up more and more neurons, bouncing off skullbone to keep reflecting, multiplying, feeding on itself.
==============
[1445] A sound crashing up staircases and down shafts in rippling patterns of interference and reinforcement. I stared down at the gun in my hand, thoughts dull, shots ringing and echoing in my head and through the halls.
==============
[1446] I unclenched my hand and the gun fell into the water, vanishing under the surface without a splash.

The phone made a distinct, metallic _clunk_.
==============
[1447] I looked up at its bullet-riddled surface.
==============
[1448] Inside, something was tumbling down through the pay phone's innards, dinging and plinking past metal obstructions. My gaze moved down, following its invisible path through the body of the phone.
==============
[1449] Finally, the clattering stopped. The gate of the coin return jiggled as something clunked into the slot behind it.
==============
[1450] Not wanting to, I edged forward. Part of me reached out while another part tried in horror to call my hand back, but it kept moving. It pushed the gate open.

In the coin return was a small brass key.
==============
[1451] I stared at it for a long moment. Then I snatched the key and pulled back, turning away from the bank of phones in the same movement. I slogged fiercely on through the water and down the hall, moving fast, not looking back.
==============
[1452] My ears still rang with gunshots. In the silence, that ring kept sounding almost like a distant telephone, bell clanging somewhere far behind me. I tried to ignore them, but the ghost sounds didn't fade for hours.
==============
[1453] Chapter 11

In a flooded side room half the floor had given way. Water cascaded down into consuming blackness, no lower level visible.
==============
[1454] I stepped carefully past the open door and the current rushing in, tide sucking my shins like it was hungry for them, and sloshed away fast up the hall, shuddering at the thought of that black pit.
==============
[1455] You fell into that thing, God knows where you'd land.
==============
[1456] Soon after, the hall began sloping up. The carpet went from wet to damp, and then, between one step and the next, dry.
==============
[1457] Up ahead glimmered a tiny spark of yellow, and as I got closer I realized it was a night-light, plugged into an outlet at the base of the wall.
==============
[1458] Something about it whispered of lightning bugs and sleepy summer nights, and all at once I felt immensely weary.
==============
[1459] I fell to my knees when I reached the weak light and sloughed off my waterlogged pack, then curled up around the tiny pale glow as if it was a campfire.
==============
[1460] My face snuggled into the brown whorls of the carpet like the fur of some huge indifferent beast. I slept.
==============
[1461] My body did, anyway. My mind kept marching.
==============
[1462] I dreamed waterlogged halls. I trudged. I can't say I explored, because I no longer made any attempt to mark my way or track my position. I searched for nothing, found nothing: just wandered.
==============
[1463] When I realized I was dreaming I tried to break free of the nightmare, but lucidity was slippery, fumbled away between heartbeats, and I kept losing it.
==============
[1464] I walked halls lit only by flickering sea-blue light and thought of nothing that wasn't them.

Once, in a long, straight hall of waist-deep water that never seemed to end, the surface ahead of me shifted, swirled.
==============
[1465] Something moved underneath.
==============
[1466] I stopped short, squinting, and held my glowstick high. The ripples flung its dim light back to me, bunched up and distorted. But I could make out something person-shaped under the surface, swimming toward me.
==============
[1467] The gun was in my hand: in this dream, I'd forgotten I lost it. Gripped by fear, I aimed it at the thing under the surface and pulled the trigger. But the shots went wide, from the angle of the water or some grim nightmare-logic.
==============
[1468] Whatever it was kept coming.
==============
[1469] I cringed back against the wall. The thing beneath the water was doing the breaststroke with smooth, efficient moves. It didn't break the surface and it never came up for air. Through the rippled distortions I could see no face.
==============
[1470] But as it swam past, I could see it was wearing my clothes.
==============
[1471] It didn't slow down. I pressed my back against the wall, cold sweat prickling my face, helpless to stop my head turning to watch it pass.
==============
[1472] It swam to the end of the hall and around a corner, never stopping for breath, leaving a wake of dark whorls and eddies.
==============
[1473] * * *

I woke with a parched, sticky mouth. My face was glued to the carpet with dried blood from where the piece of phone had cut my cheek. I tugged myself free, which reopened the wound.
==============
[1474] Wincing, I sat up and rummaged in my waterlogged pack for something to staunch the bleeding, still half-asleep. I'd left my soaked shoes on and my feet felt like they'd swelled to twice their normal size inside them.
==============
[1475] My glowstick had long since burnt out. The nightlight's weak yellow glow reduced the world to a dim circle of carpet, a few feet across. And I was groggy, still shaking dream-remnants from my head.
==============
[1476] So I didn't realize until I started digging for a fresh glowstick that someone was sitting a few feet away.
==============
[1477] I gasped and leapt up, scrabbling back against the wall behind me. I could see only tennis shoes, catching the amber edge of the nightlight, and the faintest hint of a body in the shadows behind them, knees pulled up with clasping hands.
==============
[1478] Someone sitting with their back against the wall, faint yellow glints in two eyes. Watching.
==============
[1479] I stayed there trembling for a moment, too afraid to either come closer or flee into the blackness back the way I'd come. I'd left my pack in the circle of light, between me and whoever was sitting beyond it.
==============
[1480] I realized I recognized the shoes.
==============
[1481] Hesitant, I cleared my throat. "Niko?"
==============
[1482] The face was so shadowed I could barely make it out, but I thought it smiled. "Hey, man."
==============
[1483] The voice was cracked, weak. But familiar. Unmistakable.
==============
[1484] I stepped back toward the light. "Shit, dude, you scared me." He made no move to get up. "What happened to you? We got separated and I didn't know what to do. Did you hear my gunshots? Jesus, I'm glad you found me."
==============
[1485] I knelt and pulled a new glowstick from my pack, but he held up a hand.
==============
[1486] "Okay if we talk for a minute first, like this?" he said. "Been in the dark for fucking ever and that thing will murder my eyes." He lowered the hand. "Cool?"
==============
[1487] It was such a relief to hear his voice again I shoved the glowstick back down, along with a vague sense of unease. "Fine. So what happened?"
==============
[1488] "Rather hear what happened to you. Tell me everything."
==============
[1489] So I did. How I'd waited at the bottom of the shaft, explored the water-soaked hallways. I told him about the call at the bank of payphones.
==============
[1490] But I left out the part with the gun, because in hindsight it felt stupid, and because I remembered he didn't know about the gun, and I didn't want to mar our reunion by revealing I'd kept something from him. Something else, anyway.
==============
[1491] He didn't say much. The yellow glints bobbed at times like he was nodding or cocking his head. But the darkness was fierce. All I could really make out were his shoes, and the hands clasped around his knees.
==============
[1492] In the pale yellow of the night-light they looked skeletal, emaciated.
==============
[1493] Disquiet crept into me, rising through the floor into my feet and up my bones. I couldn't see his face. I wanted to see his face.
==============
[1494] "Hey," I finally said, "this dark is kind of freaking me out. You can shield your eyes or whatever, but I've got to have some light. Okay?"
==============
[1495] He sighed, as if resigned. "If you have to."
==============
[1496] I reached carefully for a glowstick the same way I used to walk deliberately towards the light switch in my childhood basement, shepherding growing panic with a forced front of calm.
==============
[1497] I pulled one out, snapped it, shook it, blinked at the surge of orange light from mingling chemicals, and held it up, anxious, as the light crept toward him.
==============
[1498] The electric orange was shockingly bright, and he'd winced and held up a hand to block it out. He kept it there for a long moment as I squinted, pupils squirming. Finally, almost reluctant, he dropped the hand and met my gaze, defiant.
==============
[1499] Something was wrong with him.
==============
[1500] He was changed. Distorted. Something had leathered him, shrunken and withered his features, hollowed his eye sockets. At first he seemed like some poorly made caricature, face a twisted copy of the one I knew so well.
==============
[1501] But then I started to realize what had happened to him.

Time.
==============
[1502] He was older. Much older.
==============
[1503] I was still in the shallows of my twenties, remember. I hadn't been around long enough to see how age inscribes itself on people, crumples parents into grandparents and invalids and corpses.
==============
[1504] I hadn't seen friends lose hair and teeth and muscle tone. I hadn't loved someone long enough to find out what decades do.
==============
[1505] The Niko against the wall looked twice as old as he should have been, maybe more. He was wearing different clothes, but out of his standard wardrobe: the bowling shirt with "My Name Is BONG" on the lapel. It wasn't threadbare or faded.
==============
[1506] Something bulged from the front pocket, maybe a penlight, and his pack leaned against the wall beside him.
==============
[1507] He held my gaze, waiting. We stared at each other for a long time.
==============
[1508] I finally broke the silence. "What happened?"
==============
[1509] He took a breath. Let it out. "You can see what happened." He cleared his throat. I realized now he wasn't tired, or strained. His voice was just older. He spoke in short, clipped sentences, like breathing in too deep was painful. "So.
==============
[1510] Yeah. I'm not your Niko, man. Okay?"
==============
[1511] I stiffened. "You're... from the other side?"
==============
[1512] He smiled. "Ah. You still think there's just two sides. Sure, course you do." He shook his head. "Guess that's how it seems near the surface. A pair of possibilities. Neat. But deeper down, things get more... _tangled_."
==============
[1513] The word sounded heavy in his throat, dangerous.
==============
[1514] "What do you mean?" I couldn't stop staring at his face, and I swayed with the sick feeling of recognition and strangeness, curdled together by that fierce orange light.
==============
[1515] "There's a lot of space down here, Orion. A lot of possibilities. Most of them... aren't good." His glance had drifted down the corridor, but now it snapped back to my face. "_My_ Ryan and I, we got lost. Long time ago. Real fucking lost.
==============
[1516] We, uh. Never made it back."
==============
[1517] "Your Ryan?" I looked around, panic spiking. "There's some older version of me down here too?"
==============
[1518] He looked away. "No."
==============
[1519] After a moment, I realized he wasn't going to say anything else. And then why.
==============
[1520] His eyes flicked back to mine again, as if fascinated by them. He stared with something like hunger. At seeing my face again? At seeing anyone?
==============
[1521] "Been on my own a long time," he said, as if explaining. "Gotten used to it."
==============
[1522] Suddenly I couldn't accept any of this. "Your clothes." I shook my head. "Your shoes. No. They haven't changed. They should be worn down to nothing."
==============
[1523] He looked away again, out into the blackness down the hall. "Like I said. Lot of possibilities." He cracked a knuckle. "We weren't the only ones who got lost. Bumped into lots of other Nikos and Ryans down here. Most of them dead.
==============
[1524] Sorry to say." He cracked another knuckle, methodical. "But the clothes are fine, man. The clothes fit great." He forced out a barking laugh, abrupt and cold.
==============
[1525] I wondered how long it had taken his laugh to shrivel down to that emaciated sound.
==============
[1526] He sniffed. "You get used to it. Stealing clothes. I mean there's no Penney's down here, so..."
==============
[1527] "But how do you eat?" I felt angry, not the least because my skin was crawling at the thought of him grave-robbing other Nikos. Other Ryans. "If you've been down here so long, how the hell are you even alive?"
==============
[1528] He turned back to me again, no longer wistful but with dangerous sharpness. Maybe you've heard the phrase "thousand-yard stare" and maybe you've even seen one before, but I hadn't. It _struck_ me.
==============
[1529] I believed everything he said next, no matter how fantastic. The words were only flavoring on the truth in that stare.
==============
[1530] "There's a room," he began, voice graveling, "not much farther down from here. Different from anything up here. Bigger. A bit bigger." That laugh again.
==============
[1531] "Some stairs keep going down. And if you follow them far enough, they open up into black empty spaces. No walls. But keep climbing down and you'll come, in the end, to a floor. Step off the bottom stair onto dirt, packed down.
==============
[1532] Stretching out forever in every direction, as far as your light can reach, as far as your legs can walk. The Basement."
==============
[1533] He grinned, grotesquely. "Endless. And empty. Bits of junk now and then, I guess. Empty hope chests, half-buried in dried mud. Broken table legs, rotten lumber. Naked dolls. But mostly just endless dark, endless quiet. Endless nothing.
==============
[1534] Except for all the other stairs."
==============
[1535] "Other..." I swallowed. "Other stairs?"
==============
[1536] "Most of them go up," he said. "In spirals or twisted landings or long straight flights. Through emptiness, like the way down. But eventually..." He coughed, cleared his throat. "They lead to halls again. Rooms, carpet. Downstairs.
==============
[1537] But not the same one. Because if you make it all the way back up to the top, to the house, it's different.
==============
[1538] "I mean it's our house," he said when he saw my frown. "It's always our house. Not exactly. None exactly. But all close enough.
==============
[1539] Sometimes the foyer's a mirror image, or the front door's changed, or there's one more bedroom on the second floor, one less.
==============
[1540] Or the carpet's different, or the wallpaper, or the kitchen's smaller or there's no bricked up fireplace, or the fireplace is bigger, or there's a fish tank instead of a fireplace.
==============
[1541] Sometimes, maybe one in ten houses, I can't see a difference. But I think it's always there.
==============
[1542] "Each one has that upstairs porch room, though," he went on, relentless. "Your room. And they're all filled with your stuff. Little variations again. Sometimes your bookshelf has a copy of _Dhalgren_, sometimes it doesn't.
==============
[1543] That one I always look for. But it's your room, in every house. And your bed you climb up through to get there.
==============
[1544] "But," he added, "but you can't get out. You can't get out of any of them."
==============
[1545] "What?" I couldn't break his gaze.
==============
[1546] "Bricked up," he said. "Sealed off. Windows. Doors. Bricked up. Bricks behind the walls too. And behind the bricks. Bricks forever." His fingers drummed against the wall. "Like dead shoots, I think, those houses.
==============
[1547] Seedlings that didn't grow, didn't ever live to poke their heads into the light. And there's a lot more dead ones than live ones. Thousands of stairs that go nowhere for each that lead back up to a real house, a real universe. Whole.
==============
[1548] So you wander too far down there in the Basement, lose the stairs you first came down from..." He shrugged.
==============
[1549] "You come across other Ryans and Nikos down there," he added, "from time to time. Wandering. Lost the stairs they came down. Hoping to find the way back to a world with people and a sun and something that isn't this. This place.
==============
[1550] Something that isn't us. They get real fucking disappointed.
==============
[1551] "Sometimes I'll meet them wandering the dirt, crying, panicked. I stay away, of course. Can't get too close, like you know, or. Bad things happen."
==============
[1552] He pointed to his temples, and I flashed back to that feeling of wrongness when my double and I had almost bumped into each other.
==============
[1553] He looked away. "Course they're usually dead by the time I find them," he added lightly. "But. Your question. Each dead house has a pantry, food.
==============
[1554] Once in a while one has power, too, lit up like Christmas, and the fridge is running and cold, and there's lunchmeat and milk and leftovers inside. Unspoiled. So there's plenty to eat. Just not a lot of, you know. Ambiance."
==============
[1555] He stepped closer. "I heard your gunshots. That's how I found the right stair. Found you. Don't know what you were shooting at but doesn't matter. _You're not lost._ Are you." He glanced behind me, back the way I'd come.
==============
[1556] "This goes back up, doesn't it? To the surface. The real surface." He closed his eyes. "With light and birds, and grass, and people who aren't you or me. I can't tell you..."
==============
[1557] He opened them again and I wanted to shrink back, close my eyes and pretend I'd never seen something like that in human eyes, let alone in his, that hollowness and pain and greed and something else, too, something worse. But I couldn't.
==============
[1558] I could only stare back, cringing.
==============
[1559] "I can't tell you," he said more quietly, "what it would mean to me to find my way back up there. Orion. I can't stay down here any longer. I can't."
==============
[1560] Chapter 12

I wanted to find my Niko, but this strange alternate kept arguing against it. Impossible, he said. Like finding a needle in a haystack. Except this haystack went on forever.
==============
[1561] In the best-case scenario, he explained patiently, we'd wander until our food ran out, then with our last dregs of energy and luck find our way back up to the surface and out, empty-handed.

He didn't mention the worst-case scenario.
==============
[1562] Decamped in a small empty side room with low ceilings and walls bulging with water damage, we argued. A single weak light bulb stuck in the center of one wall made stark shadow-men play across the other.
==============
[1563] He insisted the smartest strategy was for us to retrace my steps to the base of the slide and climb back up. "The closer to the top, the fewer possibilities," he said, "the fewer choices. And fewer chances of making the wrong one."
==============
[1564] When he found out I hadn't seen my Niko since we got separated in the shaft, he grew even more convinced. "Maybe he's not down here at all. Maybe he caught himself on the way down, like you said, and he's up there now waiting for you.
==============
[1565] Worrying." He gave up convincing me. "Or if he's not, he'll realize heading back is the smart option. I _know_ he would, buddy." He tapped his head. "Trust me."
==============
[1566] I couldn't deny this plan made sense, but I felt sick. Too much was wrong. "Look. Even if I take you back up there, it won't be your world. You can't stay. If you're on the wrong side too long, you start to feel---detached."
==============
[1567] I shuddered without meaning to. "Like it's rejecting you. Like antibodies swarming. It'll kill you."
==============
[1568] He shrugged. "We don't know that. I'll risk it. Anything's better than staying down here."
==============
[1569] "It's not just that." I felt like a coward, but desperately wanted an excuse, a reason he couldn't come back with us. "You know about that sick feeling when you're too close to a twin. That's even worse than the headaches.
==============
[1570] So say we find my Niko and get you both back to the surface. Then what? The two of you get a double on campus, move in together?"
==============
[1571] "No." He sighed, impatient. "You think I haven't thought this through, all the time I've had? You help me get back up, I'm gone. It's a big planet. I've learned how to survive. I'll never get within a hundred miles of either of you again."
==============
[1572] "Wait a minute." I'd had an idea. "That sick sensation, when you're too close. We can use that to find him." He raised an eyebrow. "Okay, maybe you're right, and there's too much space here to find him by dumb luck.
==============
[1573] But you've got a sixth sense for where he is. You're like a magnet we can move through that haystack, feeling for tugs. Any twinges and we steer closer, till we're close enough to do the rest by shouting."
==============
[1574] "You're not listening to me, Orion." He was getting angry. He realized it, took a moment to collect himself. "There's a lot of space down here. You have no idea how much space. You're never going to find him. You need to accept that.
==============
[1575] You'll get us both lost. And I'm _sick_ of being lost, buddy. Fucking sick of it."
==============
[1576] He had an intensity my Niko never had---though maybe there'd been something like it latent in him, waiting for the right trauma to pull it out like a loose thread. It scared me. It scared me that I'd never noticed it before.
==============
[1577] He was right. I didn't want to get lost down here, either. I didn't want to end up like him.

But I also wasn't willing to give up on my Niko.
==============
[1578] I dug out my keys, held them up. "Look. I've been using these to mark my way. There's no chance of getting lost. And I've got plenty of food, still. For both of us. So we keep searching. Keep marking the way. Be methodical, map it out.
==============
[1579] And if the food runs low..." My throat felt tight. "If that happens, we'll turn back. But I can't give up on him yet. I can't."
==============
[1580] His eyes narrowed, and I could see him weighing something behind them.
==============
[1581] But then his face relaxed. A huge smile broke across it, and it was so familiar, so him, that when he threw his arms around me and squeezed me tight, I hugged him back.
==============
[1582] "Goddammit, man, you haven't changed at all. Okay." He pulled back, still grinning, and laughed---a real laugh, the one I remembered. "Shit. Like you'd give me up without a fight. Course not. The fuck we waiting for, then?"
==============
[1583] He hoisted his pack, started down the hall. "Come on, Ry," he shouted back over his shoulder, "let's go find me."
==============
[1584] * * *

Elder Niko was obsessive about marking our way---I couldn't blame him---so we made slow progress. But despite his initial misgivings he seemed committed now to finding his younger double. Even downright cheerful about it.
==============
[1585] We slipped into something like a rhythm, despite the surreal circumstances.
==============
[1586] He declined my offer of a glowstick, and didn't pull out the penlight or whatever from his shirt pocket, instead keeping close to me as I swung my light around, peering down all the hallways we passed.
==============
[1587] Sometimes, for a moment, I'd forget it wasn't him.
==============
[1588] Then the light would catch the hard-edged crow's feet around his eyes, or he'd ask in nostalgia-tinged tones if I remembered something that happened a week or a month ago, and reality crashed back into me.
==============
[1589] I supposed from his perspective I was like a long-lost friend at a high school reunion, so as woozy as it made me feel I could understand this behavior.

I thought I could, anyway.
==============
[1590] He didn't seem to need much light. I asked about this and he shrugged, saying he spent most of his time in total darkness. Sometimes, he said, there were long stretches between lit-up rooms, between scavenged batteries or glowsticks.
==============
[1591] My skin crawled when I imagined trying to navigate this endless labyrinth by feel, never knowing when you might step into a puddle of water, a bottomless shaft. A body.
==============
[1592] I thought of him wandering these halls in utter darkness, face placid, eyes unfocused, fingers skimming the paneled wall, the only sound the scuff of sneakers on carpet. Sniffing for rot at hallway junctions.
==============
[1593] Feeling on hands and knees for corpses and their backpacks of supplies, like a blind crab scavenging for leavings at the bottom of the sea. I thought of getting so used to this that it no longer seemed awful.
==============
[1594] That it seemed perfectly normal.
==============
[1595] As the hours passed the sense that he was keeping something from me, that something was wrong, only grew. He kept asking about the way back up: casually, like making conversation.
==============
[1596] But he wanted to know what was above the slide, the layout of the rooms before that, which pit exactly we'd rappelled down, whether we'd found the Library Chasm, which branch I'd taken off the Big Room to get down here.
==============
[1597] He was trying to reconstruct the route back out. Maybe this made sense---maybe he was just curious, or hedging his bets in case we got split up, like I had with my Niko---but behind the jokes and easy laughter I sensed calculation. A front.
==============
[1598] Performance.
==============
[1599] Now and then I'd ask if he'd gotten any twinges of feeling, hints we were getting close to another Niko. He'd answer right away: Sorry. Nope. Nothing. At one point, annoyed, I demanded he stop for a minute and really try.
==============
[1600] He put on a show of being abashed, of closing his eyes and concentrating---but I could tell it was only an act. He wasn't expecting to find anyone.
==============
[1601] Like he already knew there was no one to find.
==============
[1602] * * *

We'd come to a maze of endless narrow rooms and hallways lined with empty shelves of all shapes and sizes, like a fractal pantry.
==============
[1603] Stairs twisted up and down through shelf-lined landings, doors opening onto endless dead-ends lined with more shelves, stained and bent from past weight but supporting nothing.
==============
[1604] We poked around a space the size of a mansion, cluttered with oddly-sized corners and crannies, finally realizing the whole area was a dead end. There was no other way out.
==============
[1605] "Maybe it's time to turn back," Elder Niko said when we realized this, solemn. We were near the back of the big cluttered space, in a long narrow dead-end with twenty-foot ceilings, flimsy shelves stretching all the way to the top.
==============
[1606] The air was dry and smelled of dust. "Man, it's going to be hilarious when we find out my younger self's been topside this whole time. Lounging on a blanket in the backyard, you know, under the sky. Catching some rays.
==============
[1607] Waiting for you to get out." He laughed, and his voice sounded hollow, swallowed up by endless rows of empty shelves.
==============
[1608] His face grew more serious. "Or maybe he's so lost we'll never find him. Orion. I tried to tell you. This place is too big." He gestured around us, took a deep breath, looked chagrined. "It's a lost cause, buddy.
==============
[1609] I think it's time to give it up."
==============
[1610] He took a step toward the door, but I was in his way, bristling. Holding my ground.
==============
[1611] He stopped, looking confused. "What's up?"
==============
[1612] I couldn't explain my trembling, except for a deep-seated certainty that this was wrong.
==============
[1613] Everything about it was wrong, just generally, but a specific wrong thing was the way this place had taken Niko from me and done this to him,
==============
[1614] made him into something I couldn't understand and didn't trust, and I couldn't stand this stalemate any more.
==============
[1615] Some yawning possibility loomed before me, like I was blindfolded on a precipice, about to step forward. But I had to know. Better to fall than keeping lingering on the edge.
==============
[1616] I met his eyes. "Tell me."

"Hmm?"
==============
[1617] "Tell me whatever it is you're not telling me. Tell me what's really going on. I want to know."
==============
[1618] He frowned. "What do you mean?"
==============
[1619] "Damn it, stop _pretending_. Everything is not okay. You're stringing me along and you need to stop it. Be honest with me."
==============
[1620] "Oh?" His expression stayed pleasantly neutral. I could project on it anything I wanted.
==============
[1621] "Stop playing games." I clenched my fists. "Stop _using_ me. Look, we can do this together. You need me to get out of here. Both of you do. I know the way back, and I'll help you, but I need to trust you. And you need to trust me. Okay?"
==============
[1622] Looking annoyed, he scratched furiously behind one ear, not meeting my eye. He sighed, heavy.

Then, looking up at me with a resigned expression and shaking his head, he stepped forward, and punched me in the throat.
==============
[1623] I staggered back, pain exploding from my neck, but he stepped forward at the same time, looking bored.
==============
[1624] He punched me in the face so hard I spun sideways and slammed into the wall of shelves, something crunching in my nose, and he kept stepping forward, grabbing my wrists and kicking my feet out from under me.
==============
[1625] He twisted my arms as I fell so I landed face first, and still he kept moving with me, descending with his knee in my back so when I hit the ground his full weight slammed down on top of me.
==============
[1626] He punched me hard in the kidney, twice, grinding my face into the carpet with his other hand now somehow on my head.
==============
[1627] My mouth was open but I couldn't breathe, or scream or speak or think for lack of breathing. My throat felt crushed, my lungs paralyzed. Pain like a stab wound tore open my side. I couldn't think enough to move my muscles.
==============
[1628] Never taking his weight off the knee digging into my spine, he pulled something from his bag. I heard a rip, and was so sure it was some part of myself it confused me when I felt no pain.
==============
[1629] Something sticky wrapped around my wrists, tugging the hairs on my forearm. Duct tape. And now I did struggle, feebly trying to dislodge him, kicking my legs. Pathetic as a half-squashed bug, twitching, not realizing it's already dead.
==============
[1630] In moments he'd bound my ankles, too, and then my knees.

It had all taken maybe ten seconds.
==============
[1631] I tried to make a sound, to beg him to stop, or ask why he was doing this, but all that came out was a coarse rasp, not even a gasp. So I begged with my eyes instead.
==============
[1632] He met my gaze, then looked away, dispassionate. He knew what I was trying to say. He didn't care.
==============
[1633] He frisked me: hands patting my ass, my pockets, my crotch. "Gun," he said, impatient, "where's the gun?"
==============
[1634] I had just enough breath back to grunt a word. "Dropped."
==============
[1635] "Stupid." He cuffed the back of my head. "There's worse things than me down here. And worse _me_s." He smirked, but his hands had found my back pocket, felt what was inside. They reached in, urgent, and dragged out the key.
==============
[1636] His breath caught.
==============
[1637] He bent down and shoved it in my face, angrier now than he'd looked while beating the shit out of me. "What's this? How long ago did you find this?"
==============
[1638] My head spun, trying to think of some way to regain control. "Couple," I gasped. "Hours."
==============
[1639] "Have you used it yet? Gone through?"
==============
[1640] I didn't want to answer his questions, but I couldn't see how lying would help me, either. I shook my head.
==============
[1641] He stood up and slammed his fist down on a shelf, cracking the flimsy wood. Then he started to pace, furious. Thinking. I groaned and rolled partway onto my side.
==============
[1642] The pain in my kidney was evolving from a stabbing into a roiling burning sickness, like something inside me boiled, threatened to burst. Breathing felt like forcing air through pipes sealed with rust.
==============
[1643] "My Niko," I rasped. "Looking for me. Won't let you. Do this."
==============
[1644] "Your Niko's dead," he said, and he said it so simply, so matter-of-fact, it sunk into me like another punch. "Found him and got rid of him before I found you. I always kill the Nikos first. Makes the headaches go away faster."
==============
[1645] It felt like the room was dropping, like he'd cut some elevator cable I hadn't known was holding me up. I didn't want to believe him. I fought not to. "No," I gasped. "Bull. Shit."
==============
[1646] He reached into his shirt pocket and pulled out what I'd thought was a penlight. It wasn't. It was a finger.
==============
[1647] He tossed it onto the carpet by my face and it rolled once, coming stiffly to rest a few inches from my eye. It was cut through at the knuckle and pale and dead. But more or less the right color.
==============
[1648] "I've killed him hundreds of times," he said, sounding bored again. He was watching me, though, and as he noticed my tears he gave them a small, sad smile, as if touched by my naiveté. "And you, too, you little bitch. You're even easier.
==============
[1649] Always freeze up at first. Or if you don't, you try to grab my arm. But the same way every time, right? So that makes it simple to break your wrist.
==============
[1650] When you double over whining, it's easy to grab your skull and smash it into the ground until you stop moving."
==============
[1651] He knelt down, turning his head sideways to study my face, as if curious about the effect his words were having on me. "This time's different, though. _You're_ not lost yet. _You_ know the way back."
==============
[1652] He reached out and tousled my hair, playful-rough. "And you're going to take me there, Orion. Take me back up. Or you're going to die."
==============
[1653] He stood up again. "But this fucking key. Complicates things. You said you're on the wrong side, from your perspective. Yeah?" I didn't answer; he went on as if I had. "That means there's another you who's also found a key.
==============
[1654] The twin key to this one, on the twin side. And if that other you didn't get ambushed by his old bestie"---a wicked grin---"he'll pop through to this side soon enough. Because.
==============
[1655] You find a key, you're just a few hours away from finding its door."
==============
[1656] I couldn't see how this changed things. "Why does that m-matter?"
==============
[1657] He turned the key over and over in his hand, staring at it. "Staying in sync. Wasn't that always our theory?" It was like he was asking the key. "I think we have to. Buddy. I told a lie earlier. I don't always kill you both right away.
==============
[1658] Sometimes I... ask questions." He scraped a thumbnail along the key. "Find out where you've been. What happened before. The ones who have it worst are always the ones who got too out of sync. With their doubles.
==============
[1659] There's lots of connection points but the higher-up they are, the easier to get---misaligned. Two lasers pointing at each other, yeah? Nudge them just a bit, and instead of meeting, the beams go on forever."
==============
[1660] I thought of the tunnel with the infinite fridge, and shuddered. "And if two sides lose sync entirely... if things warp too out of true..."
==============
[1661] He made a sucking sound through his teeth, bringing it to a crescendo and then cutting it off, like a tire popping in reverse.
==============
[1662] He glanced at me, then back to the key. "That's what happened to me. My double and I, we... diverged. And something tore. Or popped, maybe. Forget lasers. Think pairs of soap bubbles, floating in infinite void.
==============
[1663] They need each other to stay stable. Our universes got too far apart and it wasn't good for them. They're gone now, or too far to ever reach. Dark.
==============
[1664] "But yours..." He grinned even more broadly. "A ripe pair. Undamaged. Still connected. To each other, and to you. You. I can follow you back into them like a thread. Like a fucking thread, Orion. Up and out and back and into the light."
==============
[1665] This is the part where if I was a spy or an action hero, I'd be secretly digging a knife out of my pocket, working my way free of the bonds, taking advantage of the villain's distracted ranting to try for my freedom. But I wasn't a spy.
==============
[1666] I was a Bio major. I'd never been in a fight. I was trussed up, I couldn't move, the pain was still excruciating, and I had no idea what to do.
==============
[1667] As if to reinforce my stupid squandered opportunity, Niko seemed to notice me again. Abruptly he put the key in his pocket (his front right pocket, I noticed, desperate not to be completely helpless) and dug through my pack.
==============
[1668] With a satisfied grunt, he pulled out rope, and proceeded to tie my hands and lower arms behind my back, so tight my elbows almost touched.
==============
[1669] My freedom was slipping away. I tried to keep him talking. "But..." I had to clear my throat, heavy. "If you... if Niko's dead---my Niko---isn't it too late? How can anything be in sync now?"
==============
[1670] He paid no attention to this, continuing his rope work. When he'd finished he wrapped the end a few times around my neck and fear spiked through me, but then he lifted me gently to a sitting position, leaning against the wall.
==============
[1671] He went to the pack and pulled out my flashlight, shaking it. "This thing work?" I didn't answer: he was already toggling the switch on and off with no effect.
==============
[1672] He grunted, dug some batteries from his own pack and slipped them in, nodding in satisfaction as the light came on. Pocketing it, he rummaged through my pack, eyes lighting up when he found my cache of food.
==============
[1673] He ripped open the wrapper on a power bar and took a huge bite, grunting in satisfaction. Ignoring me.
==============
[1674] "Niko," I said, trying not to cry. "Please let me go."
==============
[1675] He grimaced, like what I'd said had hurt him, and scooted closer to me, still chewing. He grabbed my hair and pulled back my head. Stared into my eyes with a frown. Like he'd lost something in them.
==============
[1676] "I told another lie earlier, bud," he said, swallowing. "Sometimes those dead and bricked-up houses do have power, like I said. Who knows why or where it comes from, but sometimes they do."
==============
[1677] I kept my eyes on his, hoping to find some empathy or humanity there.
==============
[1678] He took another bite. Chewed more slowly this time.

There was nothing in his eyes.
==============
[1679] "Power," he said, mouth half-full, "but the fridges and pantries, in all those houses? They're empty. All of them. There's no food down here, Orion. None at all."
==============
[1680] I couldn't stop trembling. I couldn't look away from his eyes.
==============
[1681] He swallowed again, shoved the last of the bar into his mouth. Still gripping me with his other hand, he turned my head from side to side, like he was admiring it. "But you and me," he said, mouth full, "other versions.
==============
[1682] Man, there's _so many_ of us. Popping up or tripping down those stairs, those millions of stairs. Lost. Always lost. Pathetic. Eaten all their food. Starving, out of their minds. They're already dead, really. Or a nudge away."
==============
[1683] He swallowed the last of the power bar, licked his lips and the crumbs off his fingers. Then he leaned forward, slow, like he was going in for a kiss.

He stopped, face inches from mine.
==============
[1684] "Wouldn't it be such a waste?" His breath smelled of processed figs. "Such a shame for all those deaths to have been for nothing. To have served no purpose. Don't you think?"

"Niko," I begged, wanting it to mean so many things.
==============
[1685] His finger touched my lips. "I think you get it. So. We have to find the door this key connects to. We have to wait for your doubles to come through---yours, and your dead friend's. Swap places with them. Pass back to your side.
==============
[1686] Keep things _synchronous_. And then head up, up, up into the shallows, back to the surface, away from this place forever, and synchronicity can go fuck itself." He stood up, reaching down, and grabbed my shirt to jerk me to my feet.
==============
[1687] He wrapped the end of the rope around his arm.
==============
[1688] "But we'd better get moving. Cause your door's going to be farther down from here. And best for both of us if we find it before I get too fucking hungry." He gestured back toward the way out of the jumbled maze of shelves, mockingly polite.
==============
[1689] "After you, amigo."
==============
[1690] Chapter 13

Like a bitter parody of the exploring I'd done with my Niko, a million years ago, we kept moving. I led, Niko following behind holding the rope wound around my neck.
==============
[1691] He'd cut the duct tape from my ankles so I could walk, but tied a blindfold made from a damp shirt tight around my face. "Little handicap," he said, "case you decide to wander off." I cringed when he clapped me playfully on the back.
==============
[1692] "Don't worry, bud. If you're good, I'll tell you when you're about to walk into a pit."
==============
[1693] We searched. At intersections he'd describe each hallway, and casually discuss which way to go, as if we were equals. As if he hadn't threatened to kill me and worse.
==============
[1694] Other than a preference for moving toward anything weird or different, he seemed content to let me choose the direction.
==============
[1695] He marked the wall, tracing our path with fastidious care---"If we're doing it on this side, they're doing it on theirs, too"---and on the whole seemed downright cheerful.
==============
[1696] For a while he whistled something I finally placed as the theme to one of our favorite shows. Just the second bar, over and over again.

Like he'd forgotten the rest.
==============
[1697] From his descriptions, I gathered we were passing through a maze of identical drab halls.
==============
[1698] The carpet underfoot was sometimes dry, sometimes thick with something that felt like dead mulch and made me stumble, and often slick with slime and mold.
==============
[1699] We must have been only just above the water table, if such a concept made sense down here. Probably it didn't. Sometimes we'd go up dry stairs to a soaked hall at the top, or along a downward slant that went from squelchy to dusty.
==============
[1700] We were near water, anyway, moving through histories of past inundation. Niko described walls streaked with damage from it, paint browned and peeling.
==============
[1701] There were few side rooms here, but he'd open the door to each we passed and check it. Bedroom-sized, he told me, all empty except for a small drain in the center of each floor.
==============
[1702] It was hard to keep my balance, blindfolded and with arms bound behind me, and I stumbled a lot. The adrenaline from earlier had worn off, leaving behind a dozen throbbing aches and a deep exhaustion. How long had I been down here?
==============
[1703] I couldn't come up with a number, but my body knew the answer. Too long.
==============
[1704] At the next intersection I tripped on a rough patch of carpet and collapsed, smacking my chin against the ground. It hurt, and I started crying. Sobbing, actually. I'd never felt more useless, pathetic.
==============
[1705] Niko told me to shut up, and I tried to pull myself together. He sighed, and suggested we take a rest. Sniffling, I agreed.
==============
[1706] He sat me up against a wall and fed me a power bar, one torn-off piece at a time. I clenched and unclenched my tingling hands; from the elbows down everything was numb. After a while the tears stopped.
==============
[1707] I wanted to sleep but couldn't bear waking back up to this. I wanted him to untie me, unwind the rope from my neck, let me go. I wanted to get away from him, or better yet for none of this to ever have happened at all.
==============
[1708] I wanted to be dreaming of something other than hallways, and him.
==============
[1709] I could have none of these things. But he hadn't gagged me. I could still talk. And maybe talking together, like we'd done so much, I could find a way to reach him.

So I asked him about the things he'd seen, and he told me.
==============
[1710] He spoke of a hallway twelve miles long without a single door or turn. Of a huge labyrinth of circular halls he'd mapped, pressing towards the center, until at last he'd arrived triumphant in the small circular room at its core.
==============
[1711] All that was there was a bent and broke bike wheel. He spoke of caged metal ladders climbing up through vast, dark, empty spaces, rung after rung through nothing but void.
==============
[1712] He spoke of more connection points between paired dimensions, useless to him since he couldn't find his way to the surface of any---and all _tangled_ down there, he said again. The connections always had some kind of airtight seal.
==============
[1713] Steam-filled wood saunas with a door at each end; school lockers just big enough to stand in with doors on each end;
==============
[1714] a shower, but vertically stretched, thirty feet of bathroom tile with frosted glass doors at the top and bottom, and climbing its steel fixtures,
==============
[1715] faucets and knobs sticking out at random from the walls, climbing it all the way to the top in absolute darkness.
==============
[1716] Because that was another universal feature of the connections, apparently. Your light, whatever its origin, would go out in the space between, like my flashlight in the fridge.
==============
[1717] He'd taken a burning two-by-four into one and as soon as the door shut behind him the flames simply stopped, not even glowing embers left behind.
==============
[1718] He spoke of curving tunnels made from scraps of sandpaper and carpet samples, of flooded libraries swimming with illegible books, of treacherous mountains of abandoned silverware, poised to bury you alive at the slightest touch.
==============
[1719] He spoke of vast caves made entirely of stairs: walls, floor and ceiling expanding and contracting in carpeted, ninety-degree edges.
==============
[1720] More than a decade later, the first time I saw a blocky cavern descending into shadow in _Minecraft_, I had to shut the game down, right then, turn on the lights, walk away. It looked exactly how I'd imagined Niko's stair-edged pits.
==============
[1721] Finally, he trailed off, and we steeped together for a while in the thick, unbroken quiet. I was trying to think what I could say to keep him talking, but he broke the silence first.
==============
[1722] "You would have gone wild for some of that shit, man. Wish you could have been there." His voice was wistful. "All our crazy, stupid theories. We were wrong about everything. But it was more fun being wrong together."
==============
[1723] I licked my lips. Maybe this was my chance.
==============
[1724] "Yeah. Hell yeah," I started. "Jesus, man, I can't imagine what it's been like for you." _Isn't the phrase "I can only imagine?"_ some part of my brain whispered. I shook it off. "I mean, I don't know what I'd have done, if it were me.
==============
[1725] Alone down here." I took a breath, extemporizing. "You've... done things to survive, and I mean who could blame you? Who's to say when push comes to shove what's right or wrong when survival's at stake?"
==============
[1726] He didn't make a sound, and I couldn't see his face through the blindfold. But I sensed a tide shifting. I'd said something wrong. My chance was slipping away.
==============
[1727] "_You don't have to do this to me._" I hadn't meant to say it and not with such pitiful desperation, but now I couldn't help myself, couldn't stop babbling. "We're friends. You're my friend. We're only going to survive by working together.
==============
[1728] You don't have to keep me tied up like this. I want the same thing you want. To get out, get the fuck out of here---"

"Friends." he interrupted, voice dangerously quiet. "Is that what we were? Back in the day?"
==============
[1729] My chest was tight. "Weren't we?"
==============
[1730] I heard a scratching sound. A dog itching itself. I couldn't see but had a clear image: he was scratching the hair behind his ear, head tilted, half-turned down.
==============
[1731] Something he always did right before explaining something he didn't think he should have to explain.
==============
[1732] "I've had a lot of time to think, Ry." His voice was still calm. "About our _friendship_. About _us_." I jerked: he'd rested his fist on the top of my shoe. "Why we ended up down here."
==============
[1733] I was losing him, or had already lost him, but I didn't know how or why or what I could say to reverse it. "Yeah?"
==============
[1734] "Yeah," he said, lifting the fist and letting it fall back on my sneaker. "I think maybe there was more going on than I really appreciated at the time. For. Example." He punctuated each word with a harder bap on my foot.
==============
[1735] "We only found this place because of you. Remember? Because you found it, underneath your bed."
==============
[1736] "Okay," I said, "but---"

"And _that_ only happened," he said, hitting my foot harder, "because we were both living in that house. And why was I in that house, friend? Why did I end up moving in?"
==============
[1737] "You just said it. We were friends." But something ugly was burrowing up. I shoved it down. "I mean maybe it's my fault you were there, sure, but I didn't mean to...
==============
[1738] I mean I couldn't have known... you needed a room, and so---"

"I needed a room, and you wanted to help me out. Is that it?" This time he punched my foot, hard: it ached through the shoe. "Why me, Ryan? _Why. Specifically. Me._"
==============
[1739] "We were friends," I said again, like a mantra that could save us. I was cringing back, eyes clenched shut behind the blindfold.
==============
[1740] "That's not it," he said, but then I sensed him stiffen, twist his head away. He switched on the flashlight and dim light filtered through the blindfold. He seemed to be pointing it down the hallway, back the way we had come.

"What is it?"
==============
[1741] "Shut up. Did you hear anything?"
==============
[1742] I shook my head, distant relief mingling with fresher fear. "No."
==============
[1743] Silence. It seemed to expand in my head, like those disposable earplugs, eating up all the empty space.
==============
[1744] Finally he turned back toward me. "I think something's following us."
==============
[1745] Some_thing_. Not someone. Oh. "Like what?"
==============
[1746] "You know about the other versions of us down here." He snickered. "More than you'd like to. The doubles, and their doubles from the other houses, and so on. They're us, more or less exactly.
==============
[1747] Which is why we get that sick feeling when they're close. And because they're us exactly, it makes them easy to take out. Don't have to learn their weaknesses, because fuck, you already know them." He paused for a moment.
==============
[1748] "But there's... other ones."
==============
[1749] I wasn't sure I wanted to prod, but found myself doing it anyway. "Other ones?"
==============
[1750] He shook his head. "Ever see someone watching you down here? Like at the edge of your light?"
==============
[1751] "No," I said, hair rising. "I mean... I don't think so."
==============
[1752] "If you get closer, you can see they look like us, too. Always a Niko or an Orion. On the outside, anyway." The pattern of light shifted as he swung it down each of the other hallways, then back to the first again.
==============
[1753] "When you get close to a double of yourself, you can feel it. Right? Feels wrong, somehow. Bad. Something to do with the synchronicity, I think, the risk.
==============
[1754] If the two of you see each other get out of sync, if you understand you've broken it... bad news, and your body senses it. That danger.
==============
[1755] "But. These other things. You get close to one of them, even if it looks like you, you don't feel anything at all. And that somehow makes it so much worse." He spat. "Because it means the Lookie-Loos aren't human.
==============
[1756] They look like us, but they're not, not really. They're something else."
==============
[1757] "You named them the fucking Lookie-Loos?" I was horrified. "Thanks. Not creepy at all."
==============
[1758] He laughed a genuine laugh, then cut it short, like he was upset with himself. Like I was pulling something over on him. "They _are_ creepy, dumbshit. They just stand there.
==============
[1759] They don't usually come too close, but if you walk up to them, they don't move away. They don't move at all. They watch you." He sniffed. "I mean they move their eyes, you know. To track you. Their heads. They breathe."
==============
[1760] He unscrewed the water bottle and took a swig. "But they don't respond to anything you do. _Anything._"
==============
[1761] He paused, as if to let that sink in. Or as if remembering something.
==============
[1762] "And if you walk off," he continued, "they'll follow you. At a distance. But if you stay in one place for too long, sometimes. Sometimes. They kind of creep up on you. Slow. Edge a tiny bit forward every now and then.
==============
[1763] Like they're eager, but also real, real patient. I woke up one time and two of them, two Nikos, were bent over me. Standing there for fuck knows how long while I slept. Staring. Mona Lisa smiles."
==============
[1764] He shrugged. "If you sprint for a while, take some twists and turns, you can shake them. Creepy, yeah, but not a problem."
==============
[1765] _Oh well that's fine then._ "What are they?"
==============
[1766] "No idea." He laughed that hollow bark-laugh again. "Maybe echoes, or waves, or something. Waves and particles. Superimpositions. This whole place, Downstairs, it's like some kind of huge multiplier. You've figured that out, right?
==============
[1767] At least that much? It multiplies. Dimensions, people. Rooms. Ideas. Emotions. Some kind of chain reaction that got started somehow, sometime.
==============
[1768] There's a spring down here," and he was almost chanting now, murmuring, his voice gone strange, "clear waters at the source. Deep. All the water comes from there. Very, very deep.
==============
[1769] It splits, and splits, and splits again, and keeps splitting. Thousands of times. Millions.
==============
[1770] And each stream is as big as the one it's splitting from, and they shouldn't all fit but they do, and it's wrong, it can't fit in your head, it's too big _it's too big..._"

He seemed to catch himself, stiffened.
==============
[1771] "But the Lookie-Loos," he said, in control again. "They do it too, sometimes. There'll be two of them, moving almost in sync. Or four. I think if two bump into each other, they sort of stick together, cluster up.
==============
[1772] And if those two meet others, they all join up, like a fucking molecule. Snarled in bigger and bigger tangles." He was watching me now, I guessed; I got the sense he was smirking, enjoying the effect the story was having on me.
==============
[1773] I turned my head nervously in the direction of the hallway I couldn't see. "And you think there's one back there now?"
==============
[1774] "Oh, I know there is," he said. "It's standing right there, watching you."
==============
[1775] I jolted back, lost my balance, and topped over, kicking back with my feet and scrambling to right myself.
==============
[1776] My skin was crawling and all I wanted was to get farther away, except I couldn't see it, couldn't see anything,
==============
[1777] and _what if a second one is coming up behind me---_

But Niko was laughing now, and it slowly dawned on me through my terror what that probably meant.
==============
[1778] "You fucking pussy." He climbed to his feet, grunting. "Dumb of me. If you'd wet your pants I'd have to smell it the rest of the way."
==============
[1779] I awkwardly struggled upright, stood, furious. He made no move to help.
==============
[1780] But I knew him too well. He might have been bluffing at the end, but only to cover for being legitimately scared. He _had_ heard something down the hall, or thought he had. And he hadn't been teasing when he'd started talking.
==============
[1781] At least some of that had been true.
==============
[1782] He tugged on the rope around my neck. "Storytime's over, bitch. Get moving."
==============
[1783] * * *

Walking blind into the unknown isn't fun, and gets worse when you're freshly terrified of it. I kept expecting now to walk into a body, someone standing in my way, fleshy and warm and inhuman. Staring. But I didn't.
==============
[1784] To my captor's credit, he never let me walk into a wall (or a pit), although he was sometimes rough with jerks to the rope around my neck to correct me.
==============
[1785] But I was reaching the limits of my endurance. My collapse by the nightlight felt like eons ago, and maybe I'd only slept for an hour or two there, anyway.
==============
[1786] Waves of emotion had washed through me since then, each one leaving its own high-water mark. I stumbled even over level ground. I was barely awake.
==============
[1787] Niko finally noticed, and agreed we could stop for "a sleep." He let me lie down, but kept my head covered and hands tied. It was better than nothing.
==============
[1788] It's a testament to the depth of my exhaustion that I fell asleep within moments. This time, I didn't dream.
==============
[1789] I blinked awake some time later, not quite sure what had woken me. Niko breathed quietly, a few feet away. I got the sense he was sitting up against the wall, legs folded up, and I was lying at his feet in the center of the hall.
==============
[1790] It was dark. He must have turned the flashlight off, not that I'd be able to see much anyway with a t-shirt tied around my face.
==============
[1791] I wondered if I could, very slowly and quietly, wriggle away. Like a worm out of a tackle box.
==============
[1792] He reached out and nudged me with his foot. "Don't even think about it, bitch." But the nudge was gentle, and his voice tired.

We stayed there for a long moment, listening to each other breathe.
==============
[1793] Finally, he exhaled, loud, frustrated. "You think I want this?" He sounded desperate. Near tears. "I don't. Any of it. Scaring you like this. I'm not a monster, man, I don't get off on it. I'm doing what I have to.
==============
[1794] You don't get that, I know, but you haven't been down here long enough. Nowhere near long enough."

I stayed quiet, afraid to say something that might make him angry again.
==============
[1795] He sighed. "I don't always kill you, either. Or at least not right away. Sometimes, first. For old times' sake, you know. I fuck you."

The word _fuck_ stung me.
==============
[1796] He leaned forward, holding his head a foot above mine. His breath tickled the fabric at my ear. "You do remember, don't you? The time we did it?" He sounded concerned. "That night, after I tried to kill myself?"
==============
[1797] Sometimes when a person is stung their body overreacts. They swell up, maybe so much their eyes are forced shut. It's called anaphylaxis. Unprotected, in the Greek. But the point is it's not the sting that's doing it to you, not really.
==============
[1798] It's your own body, blinding you and destroying itself in a misguided attempt to keep you safe.

"Yes," I whispered.
==============
[1799] "That was maybe the closest I ever felt to anyone." His voice was calm, bland, like recounting a decent lunch he'd had. "I loved you so much. Not in that way, you know. Not the way you wanted me to. But I figured what the fuck.
==============
[1800] You saved me. No, not just that." His finger brushed my cheek through the fabric and I flinched. "You _needed_ me. I was _everything_ to you. That felt so fucking good."
==============
[1801] I was trying to stay motionless. I remembered a safety video they'd made us watch at Yellowstone. _If you're on the ground and a bear attacks you, curl into a ball and play dead. Don't fight back. The bear will win._
==============
[1802] I couldn't open my eyes, couldn't breathe. Maybe it was the anaphylaxis. Something somewhere was terrifying. Doppelgangers lurking in basement hallways. A camper in a tent, terrified by his own snores.

_The bear will win._
==============
[1803] His hand moved over the shirt wrapped around my head, not quite touching it, not quite pulling away. "I want to get that feeling back sometimes, you know? It's so fucking lonely here. You can't blame me."
==============
[1804] He laughed, so loud and close to my face I cringed. "I mean. Don't get me wrong. I'd prefer a girl but there aren't any down here. Just us. Only us."
==============
[1805] His fingers outlined my face. "Anyway. Doesn't work. Never works. Never the same with you." He breathed out through his nostrils and it tickled the fabric by my cheek. "I can't trust you. Any of these versions of you. Ry, Ryan, Orion.
==============
[1806] You seem different but you're all the same. Everything you ever said or did after that. Was bullshit. None of you gave a shit about me, did you? What I needed. Who I was. You just wanted it to happen again.
==============
[1807] "And the next time I tried to off myself, that's the only reason you stopped me, isn't it?" He rapped his knuckles on my forehead, through the shirt. "Isn't it, bitch."
==============
[1808] "No." It was so soft, I'm not even sure he heard me.
==============
[1809] I could feel him shrug. "Anyway, that's why I kill you, after. Case you were wondering."
==============
[1810] He sat back up, wincing. "But sorry, man, not tonight. Got a headache." He stood, kicked me in the side. "Come on. Better keep moving. We're close. I can feel it."
==============
[1811] Chapter 14

Soon the texture of the ground beneath my feet started to vary. First it went glossy-smooth, then to shag, then to changing patterns and textures of creaking wood, tile, and carpet.
==============
[1812] I stumbled more and more over bumps and irregularities, as if the floor was crumpling, bunching up as we neared some pressure point.
==============
[1813] Niko opened every door we passed now. At the third one after we slowed down, he sucked in a sharp breath.
==============
[1814] "Definitely on the right track. You're gonna need eyes for this, kiddo." He pulled my blindfold free.
==============
[1815] I blinked in the sudden glare from his light. He stood between me and the open doorway at the end of the hall. It was dark inside, though I could see something piled up jumbled in the gloom behind him. Bricks?
==============
[1816] "Take a look," he said with a grin. "I'll shine the light. But don't lean too far in. I wouldn't bet your life on my grip on the rope."
==============
[1817] Wondering what he meant, I shuffled to the doorframe. He turned and shined the light past me, and that's when the vertigo hit.
==============
[1818] The door opened onto nothing. Past the frame, the floor dropped away into blackness. The flashlight only went so far, of course, so I shouldn't have been able to tell how far down the drop-off went.

Except I could.
==============
[1819] Far, far below us were tiny clusters of lights. Irregularly spaced, but stretching out in all directions. Maybe miles down. It was like the view out the window of a red-eye, flying over suburbia at night.
==============
[1820] That wasn't what gave me the vertigo.
==============
[1821] Curving down from the base of the doorway was a complex, multi-colored structure I couldn't at first identify. My impression of bricks was wrong, I realized. They were books.
==============
[1822] A mounded pathway of them: a ribbon of books and long flat pieces of wood, jumbled up like after an earthquake, curving down and away towards a point maybe sixty feet below and another sixty from the door.
==============
[1823] The chaos converged there into a tall rectangular object, where the sheets of wood became flat and level, interspersed with neat rows of books.
==============
[1824] A bookcase. I blinked. It sat on a long narrow platform covered in junk.
==============
[1825] It was as if the bookcase had exploded, but only in one direction,
==============
[1826] toward us: books and shelves multiplying and propagating outward and upward in an ever-widening wave of fractal repetition, connecting the bookcase to our hallway with a web of itselfness.
==============
[1827] "It's a Confusion," Niko said with a satisfied grin. "Means we're real close now."
==============
[1828] "A what?" I backed away from the horrifying drop-off.
==============
[1829] "What I call them." He shrugged. "Most of Downstairs tends to follow normal architectural rules. Walls, floor, ceiling, measurements more or less what you'd expect. Bedroom objects in bedrooms."
==============
[1830] He played his light along the path of books, embossed titles and snatches of cover art bouncing it back. "But close to a connection point, things get jumbled up. Like it's harder to maintain the semblance of order, for some reason."
==============
[1831] I thought of our fridge, in a kitchen with a pool that had a door at the bottom.

"This one," he added, frowning down, "is pretty fucking weird, though."
==============
[1832] Still struggling with vertigo (tipping forward, arms bound, unable to stop myself as I plummeted past that cloud of books and tumbled into blackness) I followed his gaze.
==============
[1833] The stream of book-stuff converged at what I'd at first seen as a narrow strip of ground some way below and in front of us, itself suspended over that awful drop.
==============
[1834] But as I focused on the strip of ground, I realized it wasn't a flat surface, but something more complex: a sort of huge tube or pipe, maybe thirty feet thick, stretching away in both directions.
==============
[1835] It made slow, lazy curves as it went, like an immense statue of a snake slithering through grass. You could walk flat along the top of the snake's back in either direction, assuming you could get down there in the first place.
==============
[1836] Its endpoints, if any, were lost in darkness.

And it got weirder.
==============
[1837] The tube appeared to be made of the same scuffed, dusty hardwood floor tiles as my bedroom. A profusion of tatty throw rugs clung flat to its surface even on the curving sides, like stickers on a tipped-over water bottle.
==============
[1838] And a motley collection of bedroom furniture was scattered all around it, also attached in some gravity-defying way to the curved surface. No matter the angle, the furniture rose from the hardwood tube as if down was towards its center.
==============
[1839] A dresser canted at a forty-five degree angle; the top of a bookshelf poked up around the edge of the curve, like peering over the horizon of a tiny planet.
==============
[1840] So yeah, picture looking down at a giant snake that had somehow coated itself in superglue and slithered through a secondhand furniture store,
==============
[1841] encrusting itself with beds, nightstands, dressers, floor lamps (some lit), bookshelves, bureaus, trashcans, and laundry hampers.
==============
[1842] Escher's own frat house. And all suspended over a miles-high drop down to god knows where, connected to us via an exploded pathway of library.

"Holy shit," I said.
==============
[1843] He laughed. "Damn straight. Okay then. Who wants to go first?"
==============
[1844] * * *

It was me. Surprise. Niko realized he'd have to untie my hands for me to climb down, and if he went first, there'd be nothing to stop me running off back the way we'd come.
==============
[1845] I'd be running in the wrong direction, away from the supposed portal back to my own side, but I felt like that might be preferable to being the prisoner of a hungry psychopath who looked like a strung-out version of my dead best friend.
==============
[1846] Of course, if I went first there'd be nothing to stop me running off along the impossible bedroom-tube, either. Except I'd have exactly two directions to choose from and Niko would have a birds-eye view on which one I picked.
==============
[1847] Academic, anyway: he retied the rope around my ankle, let out enough slack for me to get down, and wound the other end around the doorknob of the last room back, a few paces up the hall.
==============
[1848] "This probably won't hold your weight," he added, tugging the rope experimentally. "Not for long anyway. But if I brace myself and take some of the load, it should be enough."
==============
[1849] He explained the plan while sliding fresh batteries into a headlamp and tightening it onto my head: I would climb down the ribbon of books and shelving while he and the doorknob stood ready to catch me if I fell.
==============
[1850] When I got to the top of the tube-path---the back of the snake---he'd retie the rope to himself, and follow me down while I braced from below.
==============
[1851] He reminded me that since we'd be tied together, catching him if he fell would be in our mutual interest.
==============
[1852] He also mentioned, quite casually, that he had no plans to kill me. Our deal held. Once I got him to the surface, he'd vanish and I'd never see him again.
==============
[1853] If I messed with him, though---tried to untie my rope while down there and run off, or got funny ideas about yanking it---he would hunt me down. He told me of his expertise at hunting me down---me, personally. He'd done it dozens of times.
==============
[1854] He'd know which way I'd choose at intersections. Where I'd try to hide.
==============
[1855] And once he found me, he'd hurt me. He'd spend a long time hurting me.

He was an expert at that too, he said.
==============
[1856] As if to illustrate this point he pulled out a camping knife with a long, serrated blade and flipped it open: the kind you'd use to saw through small deadwood to make tinder.
==============
[1857] We'd looked at one just like it at the sporting goods store, my Niko and I, but decided not to get it. After admiring it for a moment, he closed it and attached it to his belt.
==============
[1858] I wondered if this was less a threat than insurance against being tied together above a gut-clenching drop. Maybe some of each.

He watched me watching the knife, with cut-glass intensity.
==============
[1859] "Time to go," he said.
==============
[1860] I clutched the doorjamb, trying not to stare down at the twinkling lights far below. Trying to think of some way to get out of this.
==============
[1861] "What do you think's down there?" I asked, buying time.
==============
[1862] He didn't look up, focused on a knot. "I think we're above the Basement. The soil, like I told you. The bottom."

"And... those lights?"
==============
[1863] "You find lit-up stuff down there, sometimes." He sounded bored. "Little pools of light. Oases. A pile of blazing floor lamps, jumbled together like they're having an orgy. Wrist-thick tangles of power cords snaking off into the dark.
==============
[1864] Found a ball of wadded up Christmas lights once. Twenty feet across. All blinking."
==============
[1865] He pulled the cinch tight. "Rules of geometry don't really make sense this deep, though. Maybe we're already below the Basement. Maybe this goes down forever."
==============
